古今图书集成医部全录卷四百四十一

小儿食癖门

　　　　小儿直诀 【宋　钱乙】

　　　　　癖

　　若腹中有癖不食，但饮乳是也，当渐用白饼子下之。盖小儿病此，良由乳食不消，伏于腹中，乍冷乍热，饮水过多，即荡涤肠胃，亡失津液，脾胃虚弱，不能传化水谷，以致四肢羸瘦，肚腹渐大而成疳矣。　　【注　按前证或因小儿乳食过多，致伤脾胃，或乳食起居，七情六淫失宜所致，必先调补元气为主，佐以消散之剂。若除之不以渐，则必有颠复之患。常治食积既去而热不退，或作呕吐少食，用五味异功散。胁胀少食，善怒泻青，用六君子汤加升麻、柴胡。少食体倦泻黄，用补中益气汤；手足冷加炮姜、木香；如不应，佐用四神丸。体瘦潮热口干，大便不调，用肥儿丸。若兼颈项结核，口齿腐烂，当参前疳条主之。】[1p]

Comprehensive Illustrated Collection of Books from Ancient and Modern Times, Volume 441
Children's Eating Disorders
Direct Methods for Treating Children 【Song Dynasty, Qian Yi】

Eating Disorders

If there are disorders in the abdomen resulting in refusal to eat but only drinking milk, gradually use white cakes to alleviate it. This condition in children arises from undigested milk and food stagnating in the abdomen, becoming alternatingly cold and hot. Excessive drinking of water may wash away the essential fluids in the intestines and stomach, leading to weakness of the spleen and stomach, which cannot transform and transport food and fluids, resulting in emaciation of the limbs and a gradually enlarging abdomen, ultimately leading to malnutrition.

Note: It is noted that this may be due to excessive intake of milk and food causing harm to the spleen and stomach, or inappropriate lifestyle factors from emotional disturbances. It is essential to first nourish the vital energy as the primary method, supplemented with dispersing agents. If the disorder is not gradually treated, relapses are likely. Common treatments for food accumulation when heat persists include methods for vomiting with reduced appetite, using a mixture of various flavors. For side bloating and reduced appetite, with irritability and diarrhea, use the Six Gentlemen Decoction with additional ingredients like angelica and bupleurum. For reduced appetite, fatigue, and yellow diarrhea, use the Tonic for Strengthening the Center and Benefiting Qi; for cold hands and feet, add roasted ginger and cardamom; if there are no improvements, use the Four Spirits Pill. If there is emaciation with tidal fever and dry mouth, accompanied by irregular bowel movements, use the Fat Child Pill. If concurrent issues include swollen neck glands and decayed teeth, refer to the preceding guidelines for malnutrition.[1p]

　　　　儒门事亲 【元　张从政】

　　　　　小儿肌热

　　小儿身瘦肌热，面黄腹大，或吐泻，腹有青筋，两胁结硬如碗之状，名乳痈癖，俗呼曰奶癖是也。乳痈得之绵帛太厚，乳食伤多，太热则病生于肌，太饱则必伤于肠胃。生于肌表者，赤眼丹瘤，疥癣痈疖，眉炼赤白，口疮牙疳宣烂，及寒热往来，此乳母抱不下怀，积热熏蒸之故，两手脉浮而数也。伤于肠胃者，吐泻惊疳，哽气腹胀，肌瘦面黄，肚大筋青，喜食泥土，揉鼻窍头发作穗，乳瓣不化，此皆太饱之致然也。[2p]

The Teachings of Confucianism on Filial Piety

Young Child with Fever

A young child with a thin body and fever, yellowish face, and a large abdomen may experience vomiting and diarrhea. There are blue veins on the abdomen, and the sides are hard as if in the shape of a bowl. This condition is known as "breast carbuncle" or commonly referred to as "milk blemish." The breast carbuncle arises from overly thick cotton or silk, excessive consumption of milk, and if there is too much heat, illness develops in the muscles; if too full, it inevitably harms the gastrointestinal system.

Symptoms appearing on the skin include red eyes, reddish lumps, skin conditions, sores in the mouth, and dental problems. Additionally, there can be alternating chills and fever. This is due to the milk nurse holding the child too tightly, causing internal heat to accumulate. The pulse in both hands feels floating and rapid.

When the gastrointestinal tract is harmed, symptoms may include vomiting, diarrhea, distress, distended abdomen, thin body, yellowish complexion, a large belly with visible green veins, a preference for eating dirt, a habit of rubbing the nose and hair into clumps, and undigested milk, all resulting from overeating.[2p]

久而不愈，则成乳痈，两手脉沉而紧，此其辨也。已上诸证，皆乳母怀抱奉养过度之罪。癖之疾，可以丁香化癖散；取过数服，牛黄通膈丸、甘露散、益黄散等药磨之。如不愈者，有揉癖一法。　　呪曰：日精月华，助吾手法，勑斩减消，驱毒勑摄！　　右用法之人，每念一遍，望日取气一口，吹在手心自揉之。如小儿病在左胁上，用法之人亦左手揉之；在右胁上，以右手揉之。亦吹在乳癖上，令母揉之。男孩儿用单日，女孩儿用双日。大忌风雨阴晦孝子见之。用法之时，宜于日中前，晴明好日色则可矣。
　　　　平治会萃 【元　朱震亨】

　　　　　食积

　　小儿食积痰热伤乳为病，大概肝与脾病多，肝只是有余，脾只是不足。
　　　　婴童百问 【明　鲁伯嗣】[3p]

If not healed for a long time, it will turn into a breast abscess. The pulse is deep and tight in both hands, which is the distinction. All the aforementioned symptoms are due to the excessive indulgence of nursing mothers. For the ailment of accumulation, one can use a formula made from cloves; take it several times, along with medications like beef bile for clearing the phlegm, sweet dew powder, and beneficial yellow powder, ground together. If it does not improve, there is a method of massaging. The incantation is: "Sun essence and moonlight, assist my technique; command, sever, reduce, and dispel the poison!"

For those using this method, each time they recite it, they should take a breath of energy from the sun and blow into their palms to massage. If the child's ailment is on the left side, the user should massage with the left hand; if on the right, with the right hand. They should also blow on the breast lump for the mother to massage. Boys should be treated on odd days, and girls on even days. It is a grave taboo for a filial child to witness this during wind, rain, or dreary days. The method should ideally be performed before noon on clear and sunny days.

Accumulation of Food

Infantile accumulation of food, phlegm, and heat harming nursing indicates primarily problems with the liver and spleen. The liver is merely excessive, while the spleen is insufficient.[3p]

　　　　　腹中有癖

　　癖者，血膜包水侧僻于胁旁，时时作痛也。惟癖为能发潮，为能生寒热，故疟家多蓄黄水，日久而复结癖于中脘，寒热不已，有是疾者以此。小儿脏腑和平，荣卫调畅，则津液自然流通，纵使多饮水浆，不能为病。惟乳哺失调，三焦关格，以致水饮停滞，肠胃不能宣通，如冷气搏之，则结聚而成癖，轻者用积滞木香丸，重者用取癖丸。仲阳云：腹中有癖，不食但饮乳是也，当渐用白饼子下之。如不早治，则不能食，脾胃虚弱，四肢不举，诸邪遂生，羸瘦而成疳矣。
　　　　　痞结

　　痞者，塞也。结者，实也。热气蕴于胸膈之间，留饮聚于腹胁之内，于是荣卫不能流行，脏腑不能宣通，由胀满而致痞结，势使然耳，此实热之证也。时或发为壮热，圣惠甘遂散主之。此药治小儿痞结，虽服汤药时，暂得利而滞实不去，心下坚胀，按之即啼，内有伏热诸候，并成此疾，宜疏利大便，破结散气，后宜常服进食丸。[4p]

Abdominal Mass

An abdominal mass refers to a blood membrane encapsulating water, located near the sides, causing intermittent pain. This mass can trigger tidal waves of discomfort and produce intermittent cold and heat symptoms, which is why those with malaria often accumulate yellow fluid over time, leading to a recurrence of the mass in the middle abdomen. Such individuals suffer from continuous cold and heat symptoms. If children have balanced organs and their health is regulated, bodily fluids will circulate naturally, and even if they drink a lot of water, they will not feel ill. However, when nursing is not well regulated, and the three burners are obstructed, fluid will stagnate. If cold air interacts with it, a mass will form. For mild cases, a wooden herb pill for accumulation should be used; for severe cases, a pill to dissolve the mass is necessary. Zhong Yang stated: when there is an abdominal mass, one should avoid food and only drink milk gradually, and begin taking white dumplings to flush it out. If not treated early, inability to eat can lead to a weak spleen and stomach, leading to weakness in the limbs, and the emergence of various ailments, resulting in emaciation and wasting.

Chest Oppression and Distension

Oppression indicates blockage. Distension signifies fullness. When heat accumulates between the chest and diaphragm, and fluid gathers in the abdomen and sides, the flow of vital energy becomes obstructed, and the organs can’t function properly. This leads to a distended fullness and subsequently causes oppression, which is a clear sign of actual heat. At times, this can result in intense heat. Sheng Hui's Gan Sui powder is the remedy for this. This medicine treats the oppression in children, and even when taking decoctions, the stagnation may not relieve, leaving a firm and bloated feeling in the chest that causes crying when pressed. Internal hidden heat accumulates, leading to this ailment. It’s essential to promote bowel movements, break the mass, and disperse the energy. Subsequently, regular consumption of pills for digestion should be encouraged.[4p]

　　　　　积痛

　　仲阳云：积痛口中气温，面色黄白，目无精光，或白睛多，及多睡畏食，或大便酸臭者，当磨积而痛自除，宜消积丸，甚者白饼子下之。后胃气不和，用白朮散、小沉香丸、感应丸治之。又有食积肚痛有热者，芍药甘草汤加干葛。吐者，加半夏、生姜，或加枳实亦效。
　　　　　积滞

　　小儿有积滞，面目黄肿，肚热胀痛复睡多困，酷啼不食，或大肠闭濇，小便如油，或便利无禁，粪白酸臭，此皆积滞也。然有乳积食积，须当明辨之。吐乳泻乳，其气酸臭，此由啼叫未已，便用乳儿，停滞不化而得之，是为乳积。肚硬带热，渴泻或呕，此由饮食无度，多餐过饱，饱后即睡得之，是为食积。腹痛啼叫，利如蟹渤，此由触忤其气，荣卫不和，淹延日久得之，是为气积。合用木香丸主之，槟榔丸亦可用。大小便闭者神芎丸妙。甚是斋推气亦佳。冷证下积，五珍丸亦可用。[5p]

Accumulated Pain

Zhongyang said: Accumulated pain is characterized by warm breath in the mouth, pale yellow complexion, lack of brightness in the eyes, possibly excessive dryness in the white of the eyes, excessive sleepiness with aversion to food, or smelly, sour stools. In such cases, the accumulation should be ground away and the pain will subside. It is advisable to use "Xiao Ji Wan" (a herbal pill for resolving accumulation); in severe cases, "Bai Bing Zi" (white cakes) should be administered. If the stomach qi is not harmonious afterward, "Bai Zhu San" (Atractylodes powder), "Xiao Chen Xiang Wan" (small cardamom pill), and "Gan Ying Wan" (pills for harmonious response) can be used. In cases of food accumulation leading to abdominal pain with heat signs, "Shao Yao Gan Cao Tang" (Peony and Licorice Decoction) should be taken, adding "Ban Xia" (Pinellia), "Sheng Jiang" (fresh ginger), or even "Zhi Shi" (bitter orange) for effectiveness.

Accumulated Stagnation

For infants with accumulation and stagnation, characterized by a yellow and swollen face, heat and swelling in the abdomen, increased sleepiness, excessive crying, refusal to eat, or constipation with oily urine, or loose stools being white and foul-smelling, this is all due to stagnation. However, distinguish clearly between milk accumulation and food accumulation. If there is vomiting or diarrhea of milk with a sour smell, this is due to the infant’s previous cries and feeding, resulting in a stagnation that fails to transform; this is termed milk accumulation. A hard belly with heat, thirst, diarrhea, or vomiting results from indulgent eating habits, excessive meals, and sleeping immediately afterward; this is known as food accumulation. Abdominal pain with crying, and diarrhea that is like gravel indicates a disturbance of qi leading to disharmony of the protective and nourishing aspects, which develops over time; this is classified as qi accumulation. The remedy should include "Mu Xiang Wan" (wood aromatic pills) or "Ping Lang Wan" (betel nut pills). For constipation, "Shen Qiong Wan" is effective. The same applies to conditions with cold-induced accumulation; "Wu Zhen Wan" (Five Treasures Pills) may also be utilized.[5p]

　　　　　食积冷热

　　巢氏云：夫宿食不消者，脾胃冷故也。小儿乳哺饮食，取冷过度，冷气积于脾胃，胃为水谷之海，脾气磨而消之，胃气调和则乳哺消化，脾伤于冷则宿食不消。脉沉者，伤食不化故也。亦有伤乳伤食而身热者，惟肚腹之热尤甚。人之伤积肚热，粪极臭酸，而夜间有热，伤积之明验，人所未晓也。冷者消食丸、木香丸。夜间有热，天明复凉，乃是伤寒夹食失解故也，当服白饼子，先与微利，次与参苏饮；发热，地骨皮饮、秦艽散退热而安。有实热者，大柴胡汤去大黄亦可服。《伤寒论》：人病有宿食，何以别之？师曰：寸口脉浮而大，按之反濇，故知有宿食，当下之，宜大承气汤。其喘而发热者，紫霜丸主之。冷证用进食丸尤佳。亦治食厥，乃四肢逆冷面色青黑是也，或当吐而苏。有痰者温胆汤加减服，痰定而呕自痊。冷证丁香丸可服，白饼子下痰亦可。[6p]

Food Accumulation and Cold

Chao Shi said: The inability to digest food is due to the coldness of the spleen and stomach. Infants, when fed, often intake excessive coldness, leading to cold energy accumulating in the spleen and stomach. The stomach is the sea for water and grains; when the spleen's energy is hindered, digestion is impaired. If the stomach's energy is harmonious, then milk and food can be digested, but cold damages the spleen, resulting in undigested food. A deep pulse indicates that the food is not transforming. There are also cases where the body heats up due to the harm from milk and food; the heat in the abdomen is particularly severe, causing extremely foul and sour stools, especially pronounced at night—a manifestation of accumulation that many do not understand.

For cold conditions, one can use digestion pills or lignum aloes pills. If there is heat at night and it cools down by morning, this is due to a combination of cold damage and food stagnation; one should take white pancakes, starting with a small quantity, followed by ginseng and perilla drink. For fevers, one can use earth bone skin decoction or Qin Jiao powder to reduce heat and calm the body. In cases of excess heat, Da Chai Hu decoction, minus the rhubarb, can also be used.

In the "Treatise on Cold Damage": When a person is ill with undigested food, how can it be distinguished? The teacher said: The pulse at the wrist is floating and large; when pressed, it feels hollow, indicating the presence of undigested food, which should be purged using Da Chengqi decoction. For wheezing and fever, Zi Shuang pills are the main treatment. For cold conditions, digestion pills are especially effective. This also treats food stagnation, where the limbs feel cold and the complexion appears bluish-black; it may require vomiting to recover. For those with phlegm, Wen Dan decoction can be modified and taken; once the phlegm is settled, spontaneous vomiting leads to recovery. For cold conditions, clove pills may be taken; white pancakes are also effective at relieving phlegm.[6p]

　　　　　胃气不和虚冷

　　仲阳云：胃气不和，面光白无精光，口中气冷，不思食，吐水，肌瘦虚弱，腹痛，当补脾，益黄散主之。凡人以胃气为本，惟治病亦然。胃气有实有虚，实者则有痞满内热之证，虚则有呕吐不食之证。虚者益之，实者损之，欲得其平则可矣。平胃散、观音散、银白散壮胃之剂，不可缺也。
　　　　伤寒六书 【明　陶华】

　　　　　伤食

　　海藏云：伤食宜以药下之者，当详其所伤何物，生硬寒热不等，不可遽用巴豆之类大毒之药下之。升麻葛根汤，太阳阳明也。惺惺散，风热，咽不利，脾不和，少阳渴，小便不利也。小柴胡汤，往来寒热，胸胁微痛，少阳也。然欲知其经，当以脉别之。[7p]

Imbalance of Stomach Qi and Coldness

Zhong Yang said: When the stomach qi is imbalanced, the face appears pale and lacks vitality, there is a cold sensation in the mouth, no appetite, possible vomiting of water, weakness and thinness of the body, and abdominal pain. One should tonify the spleen and use Yihuang San to remedy this. For everyone, the stomach qi is fundamental; treating diseases is the same. Stomach qi can be either deficient or excessive; in excess, there can be symptoms of distention and internal heat, while deficiency can present as vomiting and lack of appetite. Treat deficiencies with tonics, and excesses with reductions; to achieve balance is the goal. Ping Wei San, Guanyin San, and Yinbai San are important formulas for strengthening the stomach and should not be neglected.

Food Injury

Hai Zang said: For injuries caused by food, one should use medicine to purge, paying close attention to what type of food caused the harm, recognizing that injuries can vary from hard to cold and hot. One should not hastily use highly toxic medicines like Ba Dou. Sheng Ma Ge Gen Tang is suitable for the yangming and taiyang phases. Xing Xing San is for wind-heat conditions, with difficulties in the throat, disharmony in the spleen, dryness, and difficulty in urination, correlating to the shaoyang. Xiao Chai Hu Tang should be used when there are alternating chills and fever, slight pain in the chest and flanks, indicating the shaoyang phase. However, to discern the specific condition, one must rely on the pulse diagnosis.[7p]

　　　　保婴撮要 【明　薛铠】

　　　　　不乳食

　　经曰：胃为水谷之海，六腑之大源也。人身气血腑脏，俱由胃气而生，故东垣之法，一以脾胃为主，所谓补肾不若补脾，正此意也。在小儿虽得乳食，水谷之气未全，尤仗胃气，胃气一虚，则四脏俱失所养矣。故丹溪谓小儿多肝脾之疾也。若面色晃白，目无精光，口中气冷，不食吐水，肌瘦腹疼，此胃气虚寒之证，用五味异功散或六君子汤主之。若大便不实，兼脾虚也，加干姜温之。中满不利，脾不运也，加木香开之。喜冷便秘，胃实热也，用泻黄散凉之。命门火衰，不能生土者，用八味丸补之。禀赋胃气不足，亦用此丸。盖下焦真阳充盛，则上生脾元，自能温蒸水谷矣。[8p]

Essentials for Infant Care
(Ming Dynasty - Xue Kai)

Not Feeding

The classics say: The stomach is the sea of water and grains, and the major source of the six bowels. The energy, blood, and organs of the human body all arise from the energy of the stomach, hence the methods of Dongyuan emphasize the spleen and stomach as paramount. This is to say that nourishing the kidneys is not as effective as nourishing the spleen, reflecting this principle. In infants, even if they receive milk and food, the energy from water and grains is not fully complete; they rely primarily on the stomach's energy. If the stomach's energy is deficient, then all four organs will lack nourishment. Therefore, Danxi asserts that children often suffer from diseases of the liver and spleen. Symptoms include pale complexion, lack of luster in the eyes, cool breath in the mouth, refusal to eat and vomiting water, emaciation, and abdominal pain; these indicate deficiency and coldness of the stomach's energy. The treatment is to use Wuwei Yigong San or Liu Junzi Decoction. If the stool is not firm and there is also spleen deficiency, add dried ginger for warmth. If there is fullness and discomfort in the middle, indicating poor spleen function, add costus to disperse it. If the infant prefers cold and has constipation, this indicates excess heat in the stomach; use Xie Huang San to cool it down. If the fire of the life gate is weak and unable to nourish the earth, use Bawei Wan to supplement it. For congenital deficiency of stomach energy, this pill is also used. It is vital that when the true yang of the lower body is abundant, it naturally generates the spleen's essence above, thus effectively warming and steaming the water and grains.[8p]

　　　　古今医鉴 【明　龚信】

　　　　　癖疾论

　　天地气运，固有南北之殊；小儿病患，亦有彼此之异。北方小儿患癖疾者，十恒八九；南方小儿患癖疾者，百无二三。是何谓而致之？盖南方水土薄弱，饮食柔软，易于克化，厥疾少矣。北方水土厚实，面食坚硬，难于运动，厥疾生焉，亦由脾胃之不和也。故东垣以脾胃为人之主，脾胃和一疾不生，亏则百病生焉。[9p]

Discussion on Habitual Illnesses

The movement of the energies of heaven and earth has notable distinctions between the north and south; likewise, the illnesses of children vary in these regions. In the north, it is common for children to suffer from habitual illnesses, with a rate of about eighty to ninety percent; whereas in the south, the occurrence is only a few percent at most. What causes this difference? It is mainly because the water and soil in the south are weak, and the diet is soft and easy to digest, resulting in fewer illnesses. In contrast, the water and soil in the north are rich and solid, and the staple food is hard, making digestion more difficult, which leads to the emergence of such illnesses, often due to disharmony of the spleen and stomach. Therefore, Dongyuan emphasized that the spleen and stomach are crucial to a person's health; when they are harmonious, no illness arises, but if they are deficient, a multitude of diseases can manifest.[9p]

小儿脾胃本自柔脆，脏腑尚且娇嫩，为之母者，多不知调护之法，惟务姑息之爱，不问咸酸甘肥之味，瓜果生冷之物，及糍粽湿面油腻煎炙之类，诸般稠粘干硬难化之物，顺其所欲，食之过多，损伤脾胃，脾胃既伤，则不能消化水谷，水谷不化则停滞而发热，发热既久则耗伤元气，元气虚则不能运动其血，血遂不行而停滞不散，留于胁肋之间，遂成血块，居于皮里膜外，不能动移，始则有如钱大，发热则日渐长，其形如龟、如蛇、如猪肝肺者，长短大小之不一也。内有血孔贯通，外有血筋盘固，其筋直通背脊之下，与脐相对之间，有动脉之外，乃癖疾之根。夫人身之血脉，则昼夜循环无端，一周流及，此其血则贯入筋内，由筋入孔，由孔入癖。[10p]

Children's spleen and stomach are naturally delicate; their organs are still tender. Many mothers are unaware of the methods to care for them, focusing only on indulgent love without considering the flavors of salty, sour, sweet, or fatty foods. They disregard cold fruits and vegetables, sticky rice balls, and greasy fried foods, allowing children to satisfy their desires and eat excessively, which harms the spleen and stomach. Once the spleen and stomach are damaged, they cannot digest grains and water; undigested food then stagnates and causes fever. If the fever persists too long, it drains the vital energy. When vital energy is deficient, it cannot circulate the blood, leading to blood stagnation and accumulation, which may manifest as clots lodged between the ribs. These can grow larger with time, assuming shapes like coins, turtles, snakes, or even organs like liver or lungs, varying in length and size. Internally, there are blood vessels connected, and externally, the blood tends to coil. These vessels lead directly to the lower back, opposite the navel, coexisting with an artery, which is the root of the ailment. The blood circulation in a person's body is continuous, flowing day and night. Blood circulates through the muscles, entering through pores and leading to stagnation.[10p]

盖癖得血养而渐长，邪得血助而渐盛，于是正气愈惫而血愈枯矣。发为潮热，以致诸疾，或头出虚汗，或胸前项下跳动，或肚大青筋，毛焦发竖，或面黄肌瘦，四肢干枯。淹延日久，则毒气发出，变生诸证。有变为牙疳口臭，宣露出血者；有变为头面肿大，口鼻溃烂者；有变为一切疮毒流脓出血者，有变为肢体浮肿，腹胀气喘者；有变为寒热往来，似疟非疟者；有变为痰嗽喘热，衄吐下血者，有变为呕吐泻痢，脱肛下坠者；有变为心腹疼痛，疝气偏坠者，皆癖毒攻出之所致也。[11p]

Indeed, the oddities grow with the nourishment of blood, while the evils flourish with the support of blood. Thus, the righteous qi becomes increasingly weak, and the blood becomes more desiccated. This manifests as tidal fevers, leading to various illnesses: some experience profuse sweating from the head, or pulsations under the chest and neck, or distended bellies with prominent veins; hair may become brittle and stand on end, or the face may turn yellow and skin thin, limbs may become dry and withered.

If this condition persists over time, toxic energy will emerge, resulting in various symptoms. Some may develop tooth and gum sores with halitosis, or swollen faces and ulcers on the mouth and nose; others may have sores that ooze pus and bleed, or limbs that swell with abdominal bloating and breathlessness; some may experience alternating chills and fevers, resembling intermittent fevers; others may suffer from phlegm, coughing, and heat, with nosebleeds and vomiting of blood; there are those who may have diarrhea, dysentery, and conditions leading to prolapse or heaviness; or they may endure abdominal pain and hernias. All these ailments arise from the assault of toxicity and oddities.[11p]

变证多端，难以悉举，乃九死一生之病，非一方一法所能愈也。　　治之先宜针灸之法以断其根，使血不贯入筋内，则癖无血所养，癖即自败矣。外以膏药贴之，内以汤丸攻之。大抵宜补脾养气以治其本，清热消块以治其标，标本兼济。又当执其权衡，以量儿之壮弱，病之轻重。若壮而轻者，则治标之药多于治本之剂；若弱而重者，则治本之剂多于治标之药。大概肥儿丸、乌金丸、阿魏丸、千金保童丸之类，乃半攻半补平和之剂，宜对证选用，于针灸之后，可收十全之功也。医斯疾者，宜详究之！[12p]

The disease manifests in various forms, making it difficult to fully describe. It is akin to a life-threatening condition, one that cannot be cured by a single method or remedy.

To treat it, first apply acupuncture to sever its roots, preventing the blood from entering the tendons, so that the condition no longer has blood to sustain it, and it will naturally deteriorate. Externally, use ointments, while internally administer medicinal pills. Generally, it is advisable to strengthen the spleen and nourish the qi to address the root cause, while clearing heat and dissolving lumps to treat the symptoms, thus addressing both root and branch.

Moreover, one must carefully balance the treatment according to the child's strength or weakness and the severity of the illness. If the child is strong but the illness is mild, the remedies for symptoms should be greater than those for the root; if weak and the illness is severe, the remedies for the root should be more than those for the symptoms. Typically, remedies like Fei'er Wan, Wu Jin Wan, Ai Wei Wan, and Qian Jin Bao Tong Wan serve as balanced treatments that both attack and supplement, appropriate for selection based on the diagnosis. After acupuncture, substantial benefits can be achieved. Physicians treating this condition must investigate thoroughly![12p]

　　　　古今医统 【明　徐春甫】

　　　　　积滞

　　《活幼心书》云：小儿所患之证，皆因乳哺不节，过食生冷坚硬之物，脾胃不能克化，停积中脘；外为风寒所伤，或因夜卧失盖，致头疼面黄，身热，眼泡微肿，腹痛膨胀，足冷肚热，喜睡神昏，不思饮食。或呕哕噫气，吞酸，大便腥臭，此为陈积所伤；但有时时泄下清水如生草汁，是受惊而后有积，烦闷啾唧，常似生嗔，名为惊积。小儿医者，亦惟因其轻重虚实而治之可也。
　　　　证治准绳 【明　王肯堂】[13p]

Accumulation

The "Book of Young Infants" states: The ailments encountered by infants are all due to irregular nursing practices, excessive consumption of cold and hard foods, leading to the spleen and stomach being unable to digest properly and causing stagnation in the central region. Externally, they may be harmed by wind and cold, or may have slept at night without proper covering, resulting in headaches, a pale face, fever, slightly swollen eyelids, abdominal pain and bloating, cold feet with a hot stomach, a preference for sleep with a dazed spirit, and a lack of appetite. They may experience vomiting, belching, sour swallowing, and foul-smelling stools, indicating harm from accumulation; however, sometimes there may be watery diarrhea like freshly squeezed vegetable juice, resulting from shock followed by accumulation, with irritability and persistent fussiness, known as "shocked accumulation." Pediatric practitioners should treat them based on the severity and nature of the symptoms.[13p]

　　　　　脾

　　脾主困，实则困睡身热饮水，虚则吐泻生风。　　脾病，困睡泄泻，不思饮食。
　　脾胃虚寒，则面晃白，目无精光，口鼻气冷，肌体瘦弱，吐水腹痛，不思乳食，用益黄散，下利用调中丸。　　伤风手足冷者，脾脏怯也，先用益黄散补脾，后用大青膏发散。　　脾病见四季，皆仿余四脏治之。顺者易治，逆者难治。脾怯当面赤目黄。五脏相反，随证治之。　　脾主湿，自病则泄泻多睡，体重昏倦。脾苦湿，急食苦以燥之。　　实则泄泻赤黄，睡不露睛，泻黄散主之。　　虚则泄泻色白，睡露睛，白朮散主之。　　肝乘脾，贼邪，风泻而呕，茯苓半夏汤主之。　　心乘脾，虚邪，壮热体重而泻，羌活黄芩苍朮甘草汤主之。　　肺乘脾，实邪，能食不大便而呕吐嗽，煎槟榔大黄汤下葶苈丸。　　肾乘脾，微邪，恶寒泄泻，理中丸之类主之。　　凡脾之得病，必先察肝心两脏之虚实，根其源之所起，然后救疗。[14p]

Spleen

The spleen governs stagnation; when it is functional, there is stagnation with heat and thirst, while when it is deficient, it leads to vomiting and diarrhea, giving rise to wind. Spleen disease presents as stagnation, drowsiness, and diarrhea, with a lack of appetite.

When the spleen and stomach are deficient and cold, the face appears pale, the eyes lack vitality, the breath from the mouth and nose is cold, the body is thin and weak, there is water regurgitation and abdominal pain, and there is disinterest in dairy and food. Use Yi Huang San to nourish the spleen, and after that, use Tiao Zhong Wan for regulation.

In cases where there is a cold sensation in the hands and feet due to wind, it indicates spleen deficiency. First, use Yi Huang San to replenish the spleen, and then use Dai Qing Gao to disperse the wind.

Spleen diseases manifest in all four seasons and should be treated similarly to other organs. A right condition is easy to treat, while a wrong one is difficult to treat. Spleen deficiency manifests with a red face and yellowish eyes. The five organs interact oppositely, thus treatment should be according to the symptoms.

The spleen governs dampness, leading to excessive diarrhea and drowsiness, and a heavy body feeling. When the spleen suffers from damp, bitter foods should be consumed to dry it out.

If there is excessive diarrhea with red and yellow, sleep with eyes closed, use Xie Huang San. If there is deficiency, resulting in white diarrhea and sleep with eyes open, use Bai Zhu San.

If the liver invades the spleen, it may lead to wind, diarrhea, and vomiting; use Fu Ling Ban Xia Tang for treatment. When the heart invades the spleen, it presents as deficiency causing heat and heavy body resulting in diarrhea; use Qiang Huo Huang Qin Cang Zhu Gan Cao Tang.

If the lungs invade the spleen, there may be excess leading to capable eating but difficulty with bowel movements and vomiting; prepare Bing Lang Da Huang Tang and use Ting Li Wan.

If the kidneys invade the spleen, it may cause slight pathogenic effects with coldness and diarrhea; use Li Zhong Wan or similar treatments.

For any spleen illness, one must first examine the conditions of the liver and heart to assess their strengths and weaknesses, tracing the source of the problem before proceeding with treatment.[14p]

盖肝是脾之鬼，心是脾之母，肝气盛则鬼气胜，心气亏则脾家生气不足，当用平肝气益心气，盛者抑之则退，亏者益之不乏，所以有抑脾气益心气两药。诊其脉，肝心两脏俱和，则是脾自生之疾，察其虚实而治之。　　前证实者，病气实而形气虚也。若面色晄白，吐泻腹痛，口鼻气冷，属寒水侮土，宜用益黄散。若面青唇黯，吐泻，手足并冷，此脾土虚寒，用干姜理中汤。若面色萎黄，手足不冷，此脾土虚弱，用人参理中汤。[15p]

The liver is the spirit of the spleen, and the heart is the mother of the spleen. When liver qi is abundant, spirit energy prevails; when heart qi is deficient, the spleen's vitality is insufficient. Therefore, one should use methods to soothe liver qi and enhance heart qi. What is excessive should be restrained to diminish, and what is deficient should be nourished, hence the existence of two medicines: one to subdue spleen qi and another to benefit heart qi. By examining the pulse, if both the liver and heart organs are harmonious, this indicates a disease arising from the spleen itself, and treatment should be based on assessing its deficiency or excess.

If the evidence shows excess, the disease is due to excess pathogenic energy and deficient physiological energy. If the complexion is pale, there is vomiting and diarrhea with abdominal pain, and the mouth and nose feel cold, this indicates cold water injuring the earth (spleen), suitable for using Yi Huang San. If the face is bluish and lips dark, with vomiting and diarrhea, and the hands and feet are cold, this indicates coldness from spleen deficiency, suited for using Gan Jiang Li Zhong Tang. If the complexion is sallow and the hands and feet are not cold, this indicates weakness of the spleen, suitable for using Ren Shen Li Zhong Tang.[15p]

若伤风手足并冷，吐痰咳嗽，吐泻腹胀，此脾肺气虚，用五味异功散实脾气，加防风、升麻散外邪。若发于寅卯之时，用六君、柴胡、升麻补脾土平肝木。然面黄者，脾之本色也。面赤者，火生土为顺；面青者，木克土为逆。当平其所胜，以补元气为善。　　脾苦湿，急食苦以燥之，白朮。脾欲缓，急食甘以缓之，甘草。以甘补之，人参。以苦泻之，黄连。　　脾虚，以甘草、大枣之类补之；如无他证，以钱氏益黄散补之。虚则补其母，心乃脾之母，以炒盐补心。　　脾实，以枳实泻之；如无他证，以钱氏泻黄散泻之。实则泻其子，肺乃脾之子，以桑皮泻肺。[16p]

If one experiences wind-heat with cold limbs, phlegm cough, diarrhea, and abdominal distension, this indicates deficiency of spleen and lungs. Use the Wumei Yigong San to strengthen the spleen qi, adding Fangfeng and Shengma to expel external pathogens. If it arises during the hours of the Tiger or Rabbit, use Liujun San and Chaihu with Shengma to tonify the spleen and balance the liver.

Yellowish complexion indicates the natural color of the spleen. A reddish face suggests that fire generates earth, which is favorable; a bluish face indicates that wood overcomes earth, which is unfavorable. One should balance what is overcoming and tonify the original qi for best results.

The spleen is troubled by dampness; therefore, bitter foods should be consumed to dry it up, such as Atractylodes. If the spleen is in need of relief, one should eat sweet foods to soothe it, such as Licorice. To tonify with sweetness, use Ginseng. To purge with bitterness, use Coptis.

For spleen deficiency, tonify with sweet items like licorice and dates; if no other symptoms are present, use the Qian's Yihuang San for nourishment. In deficiency, one should tonify the mother; the heart is the mother of the spleen, so supplement the heart with roasted salt.

For spleen excess, use bitter orange to purge it; if there are no other symptoms, use Qian's Xiehuang San for relief. In excess, one should purge the child; the lungs are the child of the spleen, so use Mulberry bark to purge the lungs.[16p]

　　　　　脾弱多困

　　脾具坤静之德，而有干健之运。夫胃，阳也，主气；脾，阴也，主血。胃司纳受，脾司运化，一纳一运，化生精气，清气上升，糟粕下降，纳五谷，化津液，其清者为荣，浊者为卫，阴阳得此，谓之橐钥。故东垣以脾胃为五脏之根本也。脾气既弱，则健运之令不行，化生之功失职，而嗜卧多困所由生焉。法当温补其脾，脾气既旺，则腑脏清阳之气升举，易于运行，又何困倦之有？海藏用四君子加木香、砂仁、半夏，白朮倍之，姜、枣煎服，诚良法也。若脾虚好睡多惊，则是心血虚而火动之，宜安神养血。[17p]

Weak Spleen Leads to Fatigue

The spleen possesses the tranquil virtue of the Earth, yet operates with the vigorous energy of the Heaven. The stomach, being yang, governs qi; the spleen, being yin, governs blood. The stomach absorbs and receives, while the spleen facilitates transformation and transportation. One absorbs and one transforms, generating essence and qi, with the clear energy rising and the turbid matter descending. It absorbs the five grains and transforms them into fluids; the clear essence nourishes, while the turbid matter protects. When yin and yang are thus balanced, it is referred to as the key. Therefore, in Dongyuan's view, the spleen and stomach are the foundation of the five organs. When the spleen qi is weak, the commands of vigorous operation do not manifest, and the function of transformation and generation is hindered, leading to excessive sleeping and fatigue. One should warm and tonify the spleen; when the spleen qi is robust, the clear yang energy of the viscera rises, facilitating movement, thereby eliminating fatigue. The Haizang method uses the Four Gentlemen Decoction, adding patchouli, cardamom, and pinellia, with doubled white atractylodes, and decocted with ginger and jujube, which is indeed a good method. If the spleen is deficient and sleep is excessive with many dreams, it indicates deficiency of heart blood and excess fire. Hence, it is advised to soothe the mind and nourish the blood.[17p]

若因心脾气虚有痰者，宜用人参、五味子、茯苓以补心气，当归、芍药、酸枣仁以养心血，橘红、半夏以开痰。若因脾肺气虚，胸膈有痰，用补中益气汤以健脾胃，胆星天竺丸以化痰涎。若因饮食停滞而作，用四君子汤以益脾土，山楂、神曲以消饮食。若因脾虚而好睡，用五味异功散以补脾气，当归、芍药以生脾血。芍药须用酒拌炒黄，不则酸寒伤脾，此假热以对假寒也。若乳母饮酒，致儿昏醉好睡者，以干姜、陈皮煎汤解之；不应，用异功散加干葛即愈矣。　　脾胃不和，四君子加白朮一倍，姜、枣煎。　　脾困，四君子加木香、砂仁、人参各半钱煎。　　脾胃虚弱，生气多困，四君子加炒半夏曲、没石子等分为末，入冬瓜子少许同煎。[18p]

If there is phlegm due to deficiency of heart and spleen energy, one should use ginseng, schisandra, and poria to tonify heart energy, and angelica, peony root, and sour jujube seed to nourish heart blood, along with tangerine peel and pinellia to resolve phlegm. If the cause is deficiency of spleen and lung energy with phlegm in the chest, use the Bai Zhu Yi Qi Decoction to strengthen the spleen and stomach, and Dan Xing Tian Zhu Wan to transform phlegm. If the issue arises from food stagnation, use the Si Junzi Decoction to benefit the spleen, and hawthorn and shenqu to digest food. If caused by spleen deficiency leading to excessive sleepiness, use the Wu Wei Yi Gong San to supplement spleen energy, and angelica and peony to generate spleen blood. Peony should be stir-fried with alcohol; otherwise, its sour cold nature may harm the spleen, thus employing false heat to counteract false cold. If a nursing mother drinks alcohol, causing the child to become drowsy and intoxicated, use dried ginger and tangerine peel to brew a decoction to relieve this; otherwise, add dried kudzu to the Yi Gong San for recovery.

For disharmony of the spleen and stomach, the Si Junzi prescription is enhanced with double the amount of white atractylodes, and ginger and jujube are boiled together. If the spleen is burdened, add half a tael each of costus, cardamom, and ginseng to the Si Junzi Decoction for boiling. For weakness of the spleen and stomach with excessive lethargy, add stir-fried pinellia and shenqu in equal parts to the Si Junzi Decoction, along with a small amount of winter melon seeds to be boiled together.[18p]

　　　　　宿食

　　伤寒同一发热，而伤食者惟肚腹之热为甚，且粪极酸臭，夜间潮热，尤伤积之明验也。　　小儿宿食不消者，胃纳水谷而脾化之，儿幼不知撙节，胃之所纳，脾气不足以胜之，故不消也。神曲、麦芽之属，皆腐化之物，昔贤已谓能伤胃中生发之气矣，况进而三棱、莪朮乎？况又进而牵牛、大黄、巴豆乎？脾气一受伤于食，再受伤于药，至于下之而气已脱矣，所存几何？故夫克食之药，不可多用。下积之药，尤不可不审其证之可下与不得不下而后用也。　　钱氏论食不消，脾胃冷故不能消化，当补脾，益黄散主之。[19p]

宿食 (Accumulated Food)

In cases of fever from cold damage, the heat from ingested food is particularly severe in the abdomen, accompanied by extremely sour and foul-smelling feces, and a humid heat at night, which notably indicates the harm from retained accumulation. For infants with undigested food, their stomach receives water and grains, but their spleen lacks the strength to process it due to their young age and inability to moderate intake, resulting in stagnation. Substances like Shenqu (a fermentation starter) and malt are known to harm the generation of vital energy in the stomach, let alone advancing to more potent substances like Sanleng (Rhizoma Sparganii) and Ezhum (Curcuma), or even stronger ones like Qianniuzi (Vigna unguiculata), Dahuang (Rhubarb), and Baduzi (Semen Crotonis). When the spleen's energy is first harmed by food, followed by more damage from medicine, and the energy has already escaped through purgation, how much is left to sustain? Therefore, medicines intended to expel food should not be used excessively; especially, those meant to purge accumulated substances must be carefully considered regarding whether the condition truly necessitates purging or not before use. According to Qian (Qian's) discussion on undigested food, it is due to cold in the spleen and stomach preventing digestion, thus support for the spleen and the primary benefits of Yi Huang San (a remedy) should be emphasized.[19p]

　　　　　食积寒热

　　小儿食积者，因脾胃虚寒，乳食不化，久而成积。其证至夜发热，天明复凉，腹痛膨胀。呕吐吞酸，足冷肚热，喜睡神昏，大便酸臭是也。有前证而兼寒热者，名曰食积寒热。若食在胃之上口者吐之，胃之下口者消之，腹痛痞胀按之益痛者下之。下后仍痛，按之则止者补之。夹食伤寒者先散之，用参苏饮。热甚便秘者先利之，用大柴胡汤。如无外感，但只伤食不至于甚，保和丸调之。盖脾为至阴之脏也，故凡脾病者，至夜必热，热而兼寒，则又见所胜者侮所不胜矣。食未消者消之，则寒热自止；食既消者补之，则寒热自痊。若手足并冷。喜热饮食，此中州处寒也，宜温之。大便欲去不去，脾气下陷也，宜升之。若夜间或侵晨泄泻者，脾肾俱虚也，用四神丸。手足并热，作渴饮水者，脾胃实热也，用泻黄散。大便秘结，用大柴胡汤。手足虽热，口不作渴，大便不实者，用白朮散。仍参腹痛腹胀、积痛积滞治之。[20p]

Accumulation of Cold and Heat from Food

When a child has food accumulation, it is due to the spleen and stomach being deficient and cold, causing milk and food to not be digested, resulting in accumulation over time. The symptoms manifest as fever at night and coolness by morning, accompanied by abdominal pain and distension. There may be vomiting with sour belching, cold feet with a hot belly, a preference for sleep, and lethargy, with foul-smelling stools. If there are prior symptoms along with cold and heat, it is termed food accumulation with cold and heat. If the food is located above the stomach, it should be vomited; if it is below the stomach, it should be expelled. Abdominal pain and distension that worsen upon pressing should be purged. If the pain persists after purging, but stops upon pressing, it requires tonification.

If there is a combination of food injury and cold, it should first be resolved with Ginseng and Perilla Decoction. If there is severe heat leading to constipation, it should first be resolved with Major Bupleurum Decoction. If there is no external invasion, but only food injury that is not severe, it can be treated with Baohe Pills. The spleen is the organ of absolute yin, thus conditions affecting the spleen show heat at night; if heat is accompanied by cold, it indicates a situation where the stronger defeats the weaker. If undigested food is resolved, the cold and heat will cease; if the food is already digested and then tonified, the cold and heat will heal.

If both hands and feet are cold and there is a desire for warm food and drink, this indicates cold in the central region and requires warming. If there is an urge to defecate but nothing comes out, it suggests spleen qi deficiency that needs to be uplifted. If diarrhea occurs at night or in the early morning, both the spleen and kidneys are deficient and can be treated with Four Divine Pills. When hands and feet are hot and there is thirst for water, it indicates excess heat in the spleen and stomach, treated with Xie Huang San. For constipation, use Major Bupleurum Decoction. When hands and feet are hot, but there is no thirst and the stools are not hard, use Bai Zhu San. Additionally, treat abdominal pain and distension, and the accumulation of pain and stagnation.[20p]

　　　　　食积痢

　　有食饱伤脾，脾气稍虚，物难消化，留而成积，积败为痢，腹肚微痛，先调胃气，次理积，却止痢，则病根自除。和中散理虚养胃，三棱散、乌犀丸助脾化积，沉香槟榔丸、守中汤进食止痢。仍忌生冷粘腻等物，不致复作。[21p]

Food Accumulation and Dysentery

When one overeats, the spleen is harmed; with a slightly weak spleen, digestion becomes difficult, leading to accumulation that can result in dysentery. There may be mild abdominal pain. First, regulate the stomach's energy, then treat the accumulation, which will stop the dysentery and the root of the ailment will be resolved. Harmonizing the center, dispersing and replenishing to nourish the spleen is important. San Ling San and Wu Xi Wan assist the spleen in metabolizing accumulations, while Chen Xiang Bing Lang Wan and Shou Zhong Tang help with eating and stopping dysentery. One should also avoid consuming cold, sticky, and similar items to prevent recurrence.[21p]

　　　　　积病可医者九

　　面上虚肿是积。积者是脾之所系。脾主身之肌肉，故应面，故知是脾积。其脾系土，土无正形，故早晚浮肿不定，多则早浮，其睡则脾不磨，上面作肿。若病后此证，则是虚中积，宜用调脾消积行气等药。　　面合地卧是积。何以合地？其受积在脾，是冷积。何以知之？其脾好土，故知在脾。其冷者属阴，故知伤冷硬食得之，宜下热积气药耳。　　腹胀是积，其积在肺。何以知之？其肺主于气，才当受积，其气便冷，腹胀满气急，故知在肺。如腹胀先宜调气后转，转后更宜调气。　　小便如油是积，其积在小肠。何以知之？其积受于脾，脾当传心，心不受触则入小肠，小肠是心之腑，故知在小肠，则节其水道，小便如米泔油相似也。　　发黄是积，是积气伤心。[22p]

Accumulated Illness Can Be Treated: Nine Cases

Facial swelling indicates accumulation. Accumulation relates to the spleen. The spleen governs the flesh of the body, so it reflects on the face, indicating it is a spleen-related accumulation. The spleen corresponds to the earth; earth has no fixed form, which is why swelling varies at different times of the day. If swelling appears mainly in the morning, it suggests that during sleep the spleen is not functioning well, leading to facial swelling. If this condition follows an illness, it indicates an accumulation of deficiency, which requires remedies to regulate the spleen, resolve the accumulation, and promote Qi.

When the face is flat against the ground while lying down, it suggests accumulation. Why is it flat against the ground? The accumulation is in the spleen and is of a cold nature. Why do we know this? The spleen thrives in earth, indicating it is spleen-related. The cold nature is associated with Yin, suggesting that cold, hard food has caused it, thus requiring warming remedies to resolve the accumulation and Qi.

Abdominal distension is an accumulation, and it is located in the lungs. How do we know this? The lungs govern Qi and should receive the accumulation; when Qi turns cold, abdominal distension arises along with fullness and urgent discomfort, indicating it resides in the lungs. Thus, addressing Qi regulation first is appropriate, followed by further Qi adjustments.

When urine resembles oil, it indicates accumulation situated in the small intestine. How do we know this? The accumulation involves the spleen, which should connect to the heart. If the heart is unimpeded, it flows into the small intestine, which is the organ of the heart; hence, it is known to be in the small intestine, resulting in turbid urine resembling rice washing or oily substances.

Yellowing of the skin indicates accumulation, which signifies accumulated Qi harming the heart.[22p]

心主血脉，荫遍身毛发，被积气所干则发黄，故知是积伤心。宜下空心散，及取积药。此人必时复发热也。　　赤白痢是积，其积在肺，受传大肠及有外伤冷而得。何以知之？肺主西方庚辛金，其先白后赤，则是外邪。故知肺传大肠，则为赤白痢也，宜取后调气。　　两眼黄赤睛青是积，其积在肝。何以知之？肝主东方甲乙木，色青，却被积气所干，即黄赤。睛青者，眼属五脏，肝是其主，脾若受积，故令眼睛青，是肝受精。若传胆，其人口苦不要吃物，宜凉药退之。　　遍身虚肿是积，其积不在脏，只在腑。何以知之？为其积曾取后，被药发动，即不在脏，故出皮肤之间为肿也。只宜下取虚中积药，然后补之。　　多泻白粪是积，是受冷积在脾。何以知之？脾主化，受冷积在脾，冷滑而泻白粪，故知在脾，宜先转，后热药补之。[23p]

The heart governs the blood vessels and influences the hair on the entire body. If it is affected by accumulated qi, the hair will turn yellow, indicating an injury to the heart. It is advisable to administer a cooling laxative and prescribed medicinal herbs. This individual is bound to have intermittent fevers.

Red and white dysentery results from accumulation in the lungs, caused by external factors affecting the intestines and possibly due to cold injuries. How do we know this? The lungs belong to the west, governed by the metal element (geng and xin), which appears white first, followed by red; this indicates external pathogens. Thus, we know the lungs transmit to the intestines, leading to red and white dysentery. It is appropriate to administer herbs for regulating qi afterward.

When both eyes are yellow and red with a blue tint, it indicates accumulation in the liver. How do we know this? The liver is associated with the east, governed by the wood element (jia and yi), which is blue, yet affected by accumulated qi that manifests as yellow and red. The blue tint in the eyes indicates they are connected to the five organs, with the liver being the main source. If there is accumulation affecting the spleen, it causes the eyes to appear blue, reflecting the liver's vitality. If it affects the gallbladder, the person may experience a bitter taste and should avoid food; it is advisable to use cooling herbs to alleviate this.

Generalized swelling throughout the body indicates accumulation, but not in the organs—only in the bowels. How do we know this? The swelling occurs when the accumulation was previously affected; upon administering medicine, it does not involve the organs, thus swelling manifests beneath the skin. It is best to use herbal laxatives to address the accumulation and then restore balance.

Frequent watery diarrhea with white stools indicates accumulation due to cold in the spleen. How do we know this? The spleen is responsible for transformation, and when affected by cold, it leads to accumulation in the spleen that results in cold, watery diarrhea producing white stools. Thus, we identify it in the spleen, and it is advisable to first warm the area and afterward use restorative herbs.[23p]

　　　　　不可医者六

　　喘急是肺积。肺主气，其喘急则肺绝。其人当面白全无血色，故不可医也。　　面黑是肾积。其人面黑者，是肾绝也。人当不辨好恶，眼直无光，只得一日而死也。　　吐热气是荣积。其不医者，是血绝不可治也。血主心，心不能营，故出热气不止耳。　　手脚心生疮是卫积。卫者气也。胃气不生，故手足生疮。若卫绝则气不回，只得半日也。　　恶心吐干呕是胃积。何以不医？胃主化食，其胃热则恶吐，故不治。其人必食乳不化，不食亦干吐呕，面色青黄无血色也。　　泻久，住又泻，是积咬脾烂。何以知其脾烂？其人当泻白粪，为食不消，住了却放粪赤黑而死，即知脾烂，不可治。[24p]

Untreatable Conditions: Six

  1. Rapid Breathing: This indicates lung accumulation. The lungs govern Qi; if breathing becomes rapid, it's a sign of lung failure. The person's face will be pale, lacking color, hence untreatable.

  2. Dark Face: This indicates kidney accumulation. A person with a dark face is experiencing kidney failure. They become indifferent to good or bad, their eyes lose luster, and they will only last a day before death.

  3. Expelling Hot Air: This signifies nourishing accumulation. If left untreated, it indicates a fatal blood failure. Blood supports the heart; if the heart cannot nourish, hot air will continue to escape.

  4. Sores on Hands and Feet: This indicates defensive accumulation. The defense, or Qi, is disrupted. If stomach Qi is deficient, sores appear on the hands and feet. If the defense fails, Qi will not return, leading to death within half a day.

  5. Nausea and Dry Heaving: This indicates stomach accumulation. Why not treat it? The stomach governs digestion; if it's overheated, it causes nausea and vomiting, hence not treatable. Such a person will struggle with undigested milk, cannot eat, and will experience dry heaving, with a complexion pale yellow and lacking blood color.

  6. Chronic Diarrhea, then Constipation followed by Diarrhea: This indicates that accumulation is gnawing and rotting the spleen. How to recognize spleen rot? The person will pass white stools due to undigested food, then upon constipation, will pass red-black feces and die, indicating spleen rot, thus untreatable.[24p]

　　　　　积聚

　　小儿五积，为脏气不行，蓄积一处不动，故曰积。夫心为伏梁，在脐上，上攻其心，下攻胃口；脾为痞气，在胃口上横之；肝为肥气，在脐之左边；肺为息贲，在脐之右畔；肾为贲豚，在脐下。各有变动，非食之所成，乃气积也。脏属阴，故在一处而不动也。　　聚谓六腑之气留聚也。腑属肠，阳气运转不停，故其聚不定一处，发而腹痛。积聚之候，皆面黄瘦劣，嗞啀，不生肌肉，发立，或肌体浮肿，腹急多困，多为水气。　　虚中积候，凡惊中虚积者，谓因惊取复惊发动是也，所下粪青秽。凡虚中有积者，因伤食而泻又吐，如此渐虚，其病未瘥，故曰虚积也。又虚中之积，有积而频频取转，却取转不着，致其积尚伏，故亦曰虚中积。若惊积取下，则粪随惊青。如是食积即粪成块子。凡疳中虚积者，因疳病转泻虚而疳不退，故虚中尔，所取下粪里白色也。[25p]

Accumulation

In children, accumulation arises from stagnation of visceral qi, gathering in one place and thus termed accumulation. The heart is the upper support, located above the navel, where it attacks the heart from above and the stomach from below; the spleen creates stagnation in the upper stomach; the liver generates fat qi to the left of the navel; the lungs cause breathing difficulties to the right of it; and the kidneys create disturbances below the navel. Each has its movements; these are not formed by food but by the accumulation of qi. The organs are related to yin, hence they remain in one place without movement.

Accumulation refers to the gathering of qi in the six bowels. The bowels are associated with the intestines, where the yang qi flows continuously, which is why its accumulation does not remain fixed, leading to abdominal pain. Signs of accumulation include a pale, thin, poor complexion, difficulty gaining muscle, swelling, and a tense abdomen, often due to water qi.

For accumulations within vacuity, any sudden fright leads to further accumulation, resulting in dark and foul feces. Accumulation in vacuity occurs due to overeating, which leads to both diarrhea and vomiting; hence the condition gradually worsens, and the illness remains unresolved, thus termed accumulation in vacuity. Moreover, if there is accumulation that shifts frequently but does not fully resolve, it leads to further latent conditions, being likewise termed accumulation within vacuity. If fright prompts a purge, the feces follow the fright and turn dark. Similarly, food accumulation forms feces into lumps.

In cases of malnutrition (dysentery), the vacuity causes accumulation, as the illness leads to diarrhea but does not resolve the malnutrition, resulting in pale-colored feces.[25p]

　　凡婴孩所患积证，如觉一二日，先以百伤饮发表，次当归散，水姜煎服，温动积滞，方下乌犀丸、六圣丸重与宽利，后用匀气散调补。　　凡有积滞，须辨虚实。况孩儿虚瘦长短黑白，南北古今不同，不可一概论也。予今之法，实者可服进食丸，虚而微白及疳瘦者，宜服肥儿丸。　　初患元气未损之时，或腹胀作痛，大小便不利者，先用白饼子或木香槟榔丸下之，下后以白朮散或五味异功散和之。渴加干葛，吐加半夏。[26p]

For infants suffering from accumulation disorders, if symptoms are felt for a day or two, first use the Bai Shang drink to lift the obstruction. Then take the Dang Gui powder, boiled with water and ginger, to gently stimulate the stagnation. After that, administer Wu Xi Wan and Liu Sheng Wan in larger doses to relieve and unblock. Finally, use Yun Qi San to adjust and replenish.

In cases of stagnation, it's essential to distinguish between deficiency and excess. Moreover, children vary in constitution—thin or plump, short or tall, dark or light—across different regions and times, and thus cannot be treated uniformly. My approach is that those with substantial conditions may take the Jin Shi Wan, while those who are weak, pale, and emaciated should use the Fei Er Wan.

At the onset, when the vital energy is not yet depleted, if there is abdominal distension or pain and difficulty with urine and bowel movements, first administer Bai Bing Zi or Mu Xiang Bing Lang Wan. Afterward, mix with Bai Zhu San or Wu Wei Yi Gong San. If thirst increases, add Gan Ge, and if vomiting occurs, include Ban Xia.[26p]

下而热不退，或作呕作泻，饮食不思，此脾胃俱伤也，用六君子汤。手足指冷，喜饮热汤，此脾胃虚寒也，前方加炮姜、木香。面色黄白，目无精光，脾肺俱虚也，用四君子加柴胡、升麻。腹痛泄痢下重，或小便不利者，用四逆散。发热晡热，或泻未已，脾气下陷也；潮熬口渴，大便不调，欲变疳证也，并用补中益气汤，佐以肥儿丸。经云：邪之所凑，其气必虚；留而不去，其病乃实。必以调脾为主，而以消导佐之。古人所谓养正积自除，正此意也。
　　　　　乳积

　　其候但是吐下乳来有馊臭气，因啼叫未已，遽与乳吃，停滞不化而得。茅先生先用丁香散调胃，后下牛黄丸取下奶积，后下匀气散，常服健脾散即愈。　　乳癖之候，面色青黄，发渴壮热，吐乳多睡，口内生疮，渐渐黄瘦，腹内结块不散。由乳母食饮无常，醉饱过度，便即乳儿；或乳母偏卧一向，乳儿不能回转，儿亦睡着，乳滞偏于胁下，因兹结聚成块而痛者是也。[27p]

If the heat does not recede, and there are symptoms of vomiting and diarrhea with loss of appetite, it indicates a harm to the spleen and stomach, treated with Six Gentlemen Decoction. If the hands and feet are cold and there is a preference for hot soup, this indicates a deficiency and coldness of the spleen and stomach, to which add roasted ginger and costus. If the complexion is pale yellow, with no brightness in the eyes, both the spleen and lungs are weak, and the treatment is Four Gentlemen Decoction with added Chai Hu and Sheng Ma. For abdominal pain with diarrhea or dysentery, or difficulty in urination, use Si Ni San. If there is fever with evening chills or ongoing diarrhea, it indicates a sinking of spleen qi; with thirst, unbalanced bowel movements, and a desire for a transformation of the disease, use Bu Zhong Yi Qi Decoction, combined with Fei Er Wan. The classics state: where evil gathers, its qi must be deficient; if it lingers, the disease becomes tangible. Attention must be given to regulating the spleen as the primary measure, supported by dispersing and guiding methods. This aligns with the ancient saying about nourishing the righteous to eliminate what is unwanted.

As for milk accumulation:

The signs are simply vomiting and regurgitating milk with a foul smell, due to excessive crying; hastily feeding the infant leads to stagnation. Mr. Mao first used Clove Powder to regulate the stomach, then employed Niu Huang Pill to remove the milk accumulation, followed by Yun Qi San; regular use of Jian Pi San leads to recovery.

In cases of milk lumps, the signs are a bluish-yellow complexion, intense thirst and heat, frequent vomiting of milk, development of sores in the mouth while gradually becoming yellow and thin, and internal abdominal masses that do not disperse. This results from the wet nursing mother having irregular eating and drinking habits, excessive drunkenness or fullness, which impacts the infant; or if the nursing mother consistently lies in one position, preventing the infant from turning, and the child also falls asleep, leading to the milk stagnating, predominantly on the side, resulting in blockages that become painful.[27p]

　　　　　食积

　　肚硬而热于他处，或泻或呕，因饮食过饱，饱后即睡而得。茅先生用牛黄丸取积，后用匀气散调理，常服万灵丸即愈。
　　　　　气积

　　其候面色黄白，不进食，腹痛，夭矫啼叫，痢如蟹渤，此因荣卫不和，二气乖忤，日久得之。茅先生用万灵丸、匀气散、醒脾散、健脾散之类，相夹调理。　　《秘录》云：治小儿气癖，取三棱散作羹粥，以米面为之，与乳母食之。治小儿十岁以下，及新生百日，无问癎热、无辜、痃癖等皆理之，妙不可言。
　　　　　脾中积

　　面黄如土色，或面带虚浮，脐上微痛，肚皮热，饮食减少，才食便言脐上及腹中痛，所食不化，头微热。此因先食硬物或冷物，所伤在脾。治之先下青金丸取下脾中积，后用匀气散、醒脾散调理，常服健脾散、万灵丸即愈。[28p]

Food Accumulation

The belly feels hard and hot compared to other areas, and may cause diarrhea or vomiting due to overeating and sleeping right after a meal. Mr. Mao uses Niu Huang Wan to eliminate the accumulation, then employs Yun Qi San for adjustment, and regularly takes Wan Ling Wan for recovery.

Qi Accumulation

The symptoms include a yellow-white complexion, loss of appetite, abdominal pain, crying in distress, and diarrhea resembling crab paste. This is due to the disharmony of Ying and Wei, and the discord between the two energies, which develops over time. Mr. Mao uses Wan Ling Wan, Yun Qi San, Xing Pi San, and Jian Pi San, among others, for combined treatment. The "Secret Records" states: to treat children's Qi disorders, take San Leng San and make it into porridge with rice flour for the nursing mother to consume. For children under ten years old and infants less than a hundred days old, regardless of issues like convulsions or other ailments, this treatment is remarkably effective.

Spleen Accumulation

The complexion appears yellowish like soil, or with a pallid and swollen appearance. There may be slight pain above the navel, a hot belly, reduced appetite, and pain in the navel and abdomen immediately after eating, with undigested food and slight feverishness in the head. This is due to having eaten hard or cold substances, injuring the spleen. To treat this, first use Qing Jin Wan to clear the accumulation in the spleen, then apply Yun Qi San and Xing Pi San for adjustment. Regularly taking Jian Pi San and Wan Ling Wan leads to recovery.[28p]

　　　　　惊积

　　有时时泻清水如生米汁，是受伤而复有积，烦闷啾唧，常以生嗔，名为惊积。先解惊，后理积。解惊五苓散或百解散，理积三棱散或乌犀丸及三解散，炒神曲生姜煎汤调服。醒脾散、沉香槟榔丸，宁惊化积，壮气和胃。仍节冷乳，自然平治。
　　　　　虚中积

　　其候浑身微热，不思饮食，昏昧神缓，抱着一似睡未觉，肚热足冷者，多因吐泻大病及攻击之后而得此候。茅先生先用青金丸取积，后用匀气醒脾散调理，常服万灵丸、保童丸即愈。
　　　　　实积

　　其候大便不通，风毒疮疖，喉闭痄腮，咽中涎响，茅先生先用夺命散吐下热涎，后用匀气散、醒脾散调理，常服牛黄膏、天竺黄散、镇心丸即愈。[29p]

Shock Accumulation

Sometimes clear water spills like raw rice juice, which occurs due to injury and leads to accumulation. It causes agitation and frequent annoyance, often arising from innate anger, referred to as shock accumulation. First, alleviate the shock, then address the accumulation. For shock, use Wuling Powder or Baijie Powder; for accumulation, use Sanleng Powder or Wuxi Pill, along with Sanjie Powder, brewed with fried Shenqu and ginger decoction. Xingspi Powder and Chenxiang Biling Pill can calm the shock and transform the accumulation, strengthening the energy and harmonizing the stomach. Additionally, avoid cold milk, and natural balance will follow.

Virtual Accumulation

Symptoms include slight heat throughout the body, lack of appetite, dullness, a sensation of being half-asleep, and a feeling of warmth in the abdomen with cold feet. This often arises after severe vomiting, diarrhea, or illness. Mr. Mao first uses Qingjin Pill to remove the accumulation, then employs Yungqi and Xingspi Powder for regulation. Regularly taking Wanling Pill and Baotong Pill will lead to recovery.

Real Accumulation

Symptoms include constipation, wind poison abscesses, throat closure, mumps, and gurgling saliva in the throat. Mr. Mao first employs Duoming Powder to expel the hot saliva, then uses Yungqi Powder and Xingspi Powder for regulation. Regularly taking Niuhuang Paste, Tianzhuhuang Powder, and Zhenxin Pill will lead to recovery.[29p]

　　　　　痃癖

　　茅先生论小儿生下五个月以上至七岁，有结癖在腹，成块如梅核大来去，或如卵大，常叫疼痛者，亦分数类：在左胁下痛者名痃气，左右胁下痛者名癖气。下蓬莪朮散夹健脾饮与服即愈。如见面黑眼直视，泻黑血，鼻口冷，手足冷，不进食者死。　　钱氏论小儿病癖，由乳食不消，伏在腹中，乍凉乍热，饮水或喘嗽，与潮热相类，不早治必成疳。以其有癖，故令儿不食，致脾胃虚而热发，故引饮过多，即荡涤肠胃，亡失津液，胃不能传化水谷，其脉沉细；益不食，脾胃虚衰，四肢不举，诸邪遂生，鲜不瘦而成疳矣。　　仁斋曰：癖者血膜包水，侧僻于胁旁，时时作痛也。惟癖为能发潮，为能生寒热，故疟家中脘多蓄黄水，日久而复结癖，寒热不已，有是疾者以此。小儿脏腑和平，荣卫调畅，则津液自然流通，纵使多饮水浆，不能为病。[30p]

Xuān Pǐ

Mr. Máo discusses conditions in children aged five months to seven years who have masses in the abdomen, resembling the size of apricot kernels or eggs, that cause intermittent pain. These conditions are classified as follows: pain under the left rib is called "Xuān Qì," while pain under both ribs is known as "Pǐ Qì." Treating with a combination of Pēng É Zhú San and Jiàn Pí Yǐn will lead to recovery. If one observes dark complexion, direct gaze, black stool, cold nose and mouth, cold hands and feet, and refusal to eat, this is often fatal.

Mr. Qi states that in children, conditions such as Pǐ are due to undigested food, lingering in the abdomen, compounded by fluctuations in temperature, drinking water, or wheezing and coughing, resembling intermittent fever. If not treated early, it may lead to more severe conditions. Because of the involvement of Pǐ, children refuse to eat, resulting in weak spleen and stomach, causing heat to arise. Excessive drinking then washes out the intestines and stomach, leading to loss of fluids, which hinders the proper transformation of food, with a pulse that is deep and thin; the lack of food weakens the spleen and stomach, leading to inability to lift limbs, and various ailments can arise, resulting in wasting and further complications.

Rén Zhāi states: Pǐ is a membrane encasing fluid, lodged at the sides near the ribs, causing intermittent pain. Pǐ can trigger fevers and can produce chills and heat; thus, those suffering from malaria often accumulate yellow fluid in the abdomen, eventually resulting in Pǐ, and persistent chills and fevers can lead to this ailment. When a child's organs are balanced and harmonious, with proper flow of nutrients, even with excess water intake, they do not become ill.[30p]

惟乳哺失调，三焦关隔，以致水饮停滞，肠胃不能宣通，如冷气搏之，则结聚而成癖。轻者用导滞木香丸，重者用取癖丸。　　曾氏曰：婴儿始生，禀赋未完，失于襁褓之不谨，乳哺之不节，外为六淫侵袭，内因五脏气虚，冷积久停于脾，不能克化，结成癖块，突于胁下或左或右，其疾皆因积滞蕴作，致有寒热，或腹肚疼痛，或昼凉夜热。治疗之法：气实者亦须温正胃气，后用乌犀丸或水晶丹下之。如过三三次，即以稀粥略止，候所作形证消尽，方投补益之剂。气虚者先与调脾胃，固真元，神色稍正，饮食进多，如前法下之。若太虚甚，用三棱散、化癖丸渐消之，顺适阴阳，以平为期。然先补后泻，行迎夺之法。则取去陈寒冷积。若面黄唇白，发竖肌瘦，乃为虚极，不可轻下，但徐徐用药，消化调理为上。若儿小者，更令乳母常服藿香饮使药从乳过，亦少助也。[31p]

If there is a disorder in breastfeeding, with the three burners being obstructed, this leads to stagnation of fluids, and the intestines and stomach are unable to function properly. If cold air attacks, it can gather and form a mass. For mild cases, use the Daodi Mu Xiang Pills, and for severe cases, use the Qu Pi Pills.

Zeng says: When infants are born, their endowments are not yet complete. If there is a lack of care in swaddling and a lack of regulation in breastfeeding, coupled with external injuries from the six excesses and internal weakness of the five organs, cold accumulates and stagnates in the spleen, unable to transform, leading to the formation of masses. These masses may protrude beneath the ribs, either to the left or right. The ailments arise from accumulated stagnation, causing cold and heat symptoms, abdominal pain, or cooler days and warmer nights.

The treatment method: For those with excess qi, it is necessary to warm and correct the stomach qi before administering Wu Xi Pills or Crystal Pills. After about three doses, stop with thin porridge and wait until the symptoms disappear before using tonifying agents. For those with qi deficiency, first regulate the spleen and stomach, stabilize the true essence, and slightly correct the complexion. Increase food intake and use the previous method for treatment. If there is severe deficiency, gradually dissolve with San Leng Powder or Hua Pi Pills, accommodating yin and yang, aiming for balance. However, first support, then drain, following the method of receiving and expelling to eliminate cold stagnation.

If the face is yellow, lips white, hair stands up, and the body is emaciated, this indicates extreme deficiency, and one should not hastily drain but rather use medicine slowly for digestion and regulation. If the child is small, ensure the wet nurse regularly consumes Ho Xiang decoction, allowing the medicine to pass through the milk, which is also of slight assistance.[31p]

　　　　　痞结

　　此痞在腹内，与心下之痞不同，宜常服进食丸。按进食丸有巴豆，岂宜常服？甘遂有大毒，泻水如决江河，非十分壮实、十分危急、十分水气，三者俱备，未可轻用，今以为痞结主方谬矣。　　痞癖既久，饮食减少，脾气必虚，久而不愈，必先以固胃气为主，使养正则积自除。若欲直攻其结，不惟不能善消，抑亦损其脾土，脾土既亏必变证百出矣。当参各类及随见证而主治之。
　　　　小儿卫生总微论方 【宋　撰人未详】
　　　　　食气积癖论

　　小儿积聚癖症者，其证不同。积聚乃气之所致，不可轻治。脾胃既已虚冷，饮食先已不化，乳哺再稍失其宜，便乃成伤也。其候身体壮热，口中气温，面黄腹胀，目无精光，或白睛多，喜睡，四肢垂亸，畏食壮热，大便酸臭，或为吐泻，水谷不消，须宜稳药克化，不可便行快药取转。小儿气实脾胃壮者，化之有渐。若气怯脾胃弱者，但稍失调养，便成伤也。[32p]

Phlegm Accumulation

This phlegm is inside the abdomen and differs from the phlegm below the heart; it is advisable to take food pills regularly. However, since food pills contain croton seeds, can they be taken frequently? Gansui is highly toxic and causes diarrhea as if the rivers are breaking through; unless one is extremely robust, in a very dangerous state, or has a great amount of excess fluid—these three conditions must all be met—it should not be used lightly. Those who consider it a primary treatment for phlegm accumulation are mistaken.

If phlegm has persisted for a long time, appetite will decrease, causing a deficiency in the spleen and qi. If left untreated for a long time, the focus must first be on strengthening the stomach qi, so that effective nourishment can eliminate the accumulation by itself. If one desires to attack the accumulation directly, not only can it not be effectively removed, but it may also damage the spleen and earth, leading to various other symptoms due to the depletion of the spleen. Each case should be treated according to various symptoms.

Discussion on Dietary Accumulation in Infants

The symptoms of accumulation in infants differ. Accumulation is caused by qi; it should not be treated lightly. When the spleen and stomach are deficient and cold, food cannot be digested properly, and if breast milk is not administered appropriately, it leads to harm. Symptoms include a healthy body that feels warm, a warm breath in the mouth, a pale face, a swollen abdomen, dull eyes, excessive white in the eyes, a tendency to sleep, limbs that are limp, aversion to food, foul-smelling stools, or vomiting and diarrhea, indicating that food cannot be digested. Stabilizing medications should be used to resolve these issues; one should not hastily resort to strong medications.

In infants with strong qi and a robust spleen and stomach, digestive recovery can occur gradually. However, those with weak qi and a frail spleen and stomach will easily incur harm with even slight disruptions in nourishment.[32p]

　　　　方

　　紫双丸 [紫双丸　原作「双紫圆」，据《千金》卷五改。 ]【《千金方》，下同】 　治小儿身热头痛，饮食不消，腹中胀满，或小腹绞痛，大小便不利，或重下数起；小儿无异疾，惟饮食过度，不知自止，哺乳失节，或惊悸寒热，惟此丸治之。不瘥，更可重服。小儿欲下，是其蒸候，哺食减少，气息不快，夜啼不眠，是腹内不调，悉宜用此丸，不用他药，数用神验，千金不传。臣亿等详[臣亿等详　原作「今详」，据《千金》卷五改。]序例中凡云服紫丸者，即前变蒸篇中四味者是也。云服紫丸不下者，服赤丸，赤丸瘥快，病重者当用之。方中并无赤丸，而此用朱砂，又力紧于紫丸，疑此即是赤丸也。[33p]

Prescription for Zishuang Pill

This prescription is effective for treating children's fever, headaches, poor digestion, abdominal distension, or cramping in the lower abdomen, as well as difficulties with urination and defecation, or frequent urges to defecate. If the child shows no other ailments but has overeaten, fails to restrain themselves, has irregular nursing, or experiences fright and alternating chills and fever, this pill will remedy the condition. If symptoms persist, it can be taken again. If a child desires to defecate, it indicates an internal issue; when their appetite decreases, and they exhibit discomfort and night crying, it signifies a disturbance in the abdomen, and this pill should be used exclusively, without resorting to other medicines. Its efficacy has been confirmed repeatedly, and the secrets of this remedy are not widely shared.

In the detailed instructions mentioned, any reference to taking the purple pill corresponds to the four ingredients outlined in the previous sections. If the purple pill does not alleviate the issue, then one should take the red pill, which works more rapidly. Although this prescription does not explicitly include the red pill, the use of cinnabar indicates a stronger effect than the purple pill; it is suspected that this refers to the red pill.[33p]

　　巴豆霜　蕤核仁各十八铢　麦门冬十铢　甘草五铢　甘遂　朱砂飞，各二铢　牡蛎　蜡各八铢　　右八味，以熟汤洗巴豆研，新布绞去油，别捣甘草、甘遂、牡蛎、麦门冬下筛讫，研蕤核仁令极熟，乃内散更捣二千杵，药燥不能相丸，更入少蜜足之。半岁儿服如荏子一双，一岁二岁儿服如半麻子一双，三四岁者服如麻子二丸，五六岁者服如大麻子二丸，七岁八岁服如小豆二丸，九岁十岁微大于小豆二丸。常以鸡鸣时服，至日出时不下者，热粥饮数合即下，丸皆双出也。下甚者，饮以冷粥即止。
　　充悦圆　治小儿胎中宿热，母饮食粗恶辛苦，乳汁不起，儿乳哺不为肌肤，心腹痞满，萎黄瘦瘠，四肢痿躄缭戾，服之可令充悦。　　芍药　柴胡各二两　大黄　人参各一两　干姜如热以枳实代　甘草各半两　鳖甲　茯苓各一两半　　右八味为末，蜜丸如大豆，服一丸，一岁已上乳服三丸，七岁儿服十丸，日二。[34p]

Ba Dou Powder: 18 zhu of Ba Dou and Rui He Ren each, 10 zhu of Mai Men Dong, 5 zhu of Gan Cao, 2 zhu each of Gan Sui and Zhu Sha Fei, 8 zhu each of Mu Li and La. The above eight ingredients are washed with hot water to prepare Ba Dou. After grinding, strain the oil with a new cloth. Separately grind Gan Cao, Gan Sui, Mu Li, and Mai Men Dong, then sift. Grind Rui He Ren until thoroughly cooked, then add the powder and grind again for 2,000 times. If too dry to form pills, add a little honey until suitable.

For children under half a year to take double like sesame seeds, for one to two years like half a sesame seed, for three to four years like two sesame seeds, for five to six years like two big sesame seeds, for seven to eight years like two small beans, and for nine to ten years slightly larger than two small beans. Always take at the crowing of the rooster, if not expelled by sunrise, drink a few cups of hot porridge to aid expulsion; the pills will all come out as double. If it causes excessive expulsion, drink cold porridge to stop.

Chong Yue Yuan: Treats residual heat in infants caused by the mother's coarse and spicy diet, leading to a lack of milk, inability to nourish the skin, and symptoms like a distended abdomen, yellowish pallor, emaciation, and weak limbs. Taking it can invigorate.

Shao Yao and Chai Hu each 2 liang, Da Huang and Ren Shen each 1 liang, Gan Jiang to be heated and substituted with Zhi Shi, Gan Cao each 0.5 liang, Bie Jia and Fu Ling each 1.5 liang.

The above eight ingredients are powdered, mixed with honey to form pills the size of large beans. Take one pill, for infants over one year take three pills, and for children seven years old take ten pills, twice daily.[34p]

　　牛黄圆　治小儿宿乳不消，腹痛惊啼。　　真牛黄三铢　附子二枚　真珠　巴豆霜　杏仁各一两　　右五味，捣附子、真珠为末下筛，别捣巴豆、杏仁令如泥，内药及牛黄捣一千二百杵，药成若干入少蜜足之。百日儿服如粟米一丸，二岁儿服如麻子一丸，五六岁儿服如胡豆一丸，日二。先乳哺了服之，膈上下悉当微转，药完出者病愈，散出者更服，以药完出为度。
　　芒硝紫圆　治小儿宿食，癖气痰饮，往来寒热，不欲食，消瘦。　　芒硝　大黄各四两　半夏　甘遂各二两　代赭一两　巴豆二百枚　杏仁一百二十枚　　右七味为末，别捣巴豆、杏仁，治如膏，旋内药末捣三千杵，令相和合，强者内少蜜，百日儿服如胡豆一丸，过百日至一岁服二丸，随儿大小以意节度，当候儿大便中药出为愈。若不出，更服如初。[35p]

Niu Huang Yuan: For treating infants with undigested milk, abdominal pain, and startled crying.

Ingredients:

  • 3 grams of true cow bile;
  • 2 pieces of aconite;
  • 1 tael each of genuine pearls, croton seed powder, and apricot kernels.

Instructions: Grind the aconite and genuine pearls into a fine powder and sieve separately. Grind the croton seed and apricot kernels into a paste. Combine with the cow bile and grind together for 1,200 strokes. Once the medicine is ready, mix it with a little honey.

Dosage: For a hundred-day-old infant, take a round the size of millet; for a two-year-old, the size of a sesame seed; for a child aged five to six, the size of a broad bean, twice daily. It should be taken after nursing, and any sensations of movement in the upper and lower belly should be noted. If the medicine passes out completely, the child is healed; if expelled in fragments, additional doses are necessary until the medicine is fully excreted.

Mang Xiao Zi Yuan: For treating children with retained food, phlegm and qi stagnation, alternating chills and fevers, loss of appetite, and emaciation.

Ingredients:

  • 4 taels of glauber's salt;
  • 4 taels of rhubarb;
  • 2 taels each of pinellia and herbs of the sweet milkweed;
  • 1 tael of red earth;
  • 200 pieces of croton seeds;
  • 120 pieces of apricot kernels.

Instructions: Grind the seven ingredients into a powder. Separately grind the croton seeds and apricot kernels into a paste. Combine this with the powdered ingredients and grind together for 3,000 strokes until well mixed. For those with more strength, a little honey can be added.

Dosage: For a hundred-day-old child, take a round the size of a broad bean; for children over a hundred days to one year, take two rounds based on the child's size and tolerance. The dosage should be adjusted according to the child’s bowel movements, indicating when healing has occurred. If not excreted, repeat the initial dosage.[35p]

　　消痞丸
　　黄连五钱　黄芩二钱　厚朴七分　姜黄五分　干生姜　人参各四分　甘草三分　枳实二分　橘皮一分　　右为细末，汤浸蒸饼为丸如黍米大，每服三十丸，随乳下。
　　雄黄解毒丸 【《片玉心书》，下同】 　下痰去热，追虫打积。　　雄黄一钱，另研　郁金一钱　巴豆霜二钱　共为末，米糊丸如粟米大，痰涎甚竹叶汤下；积痛茴香汤下；缠喉风，滚白水化开，吐痰；虫痛，苦楝子根白皮汤下，先以鸡卵油煎，空心时令儿闻之，然后服药，必要上半月，谓其虫之头向上故也。
　　养脾丸　治小儿脾胃虚弱，不思乳食，伤食癖积，面色黄，呕吐泻泄，腹痛膨胀，并皆治之。　　苍朮制　陈皮各五钱　缩砂仁　草果仁　益智仁各二钱　厚朴　神曲　麦芽炒，各三钱　共为末，酒糊丸如粟米大，米饮下。脾胃虚弱，米汤下；呕吐，煨姜汤下；食积，山楂汤下：腹痛，茴香汤下；肿胀，萝卜汤下；寒泄，姜枣汤下。[41p]

Xiaopi Pill
Huanglian 5 qian, Huangqin 2 qian, Houpo 7 fen, Jianghuang 5 fen, Gan Shengjiang, Ren Shen each 4 fen, Gancao 3 fen, Zhishi 2 fen, Jupi 1 fen. Grind these into a fine powder, soak in soup to make into pills the size of millet. Take 30 pills each time, followed by milk.

Xionghuang Detoxification Pill (from "Pianyu Xinshi", same below)
To dispel phlegm and heat, purge parasites and remove accumulation. Xionghuang 1 qian, ground separately; Yujin 1 qian, Bazi powder 2 qian. Grind together into a powder, form into pills the size of corn. For excessive phlegm, swallow with bamboo leaf decoction; for accumulation pain, swallow with fennel decoction; for throat wind, dissolve in boiling water and expel phlegm; for parasite pain, swallow with bitter neem root skin decoction, first fry with egg oil, during fasting, let child smell it, then take the medicine. It's essential to do this for half a month, for it is said that the heads of the parasites face upwards.

Yangpi Pill
For treating infants with weak spleen and stomach, lack of appetite for milk and food, food accumulation, yellow complexion, vomiting, diarrhea, abdominal pain, and bloating.
Cangzhu and Chenpi each 5 qian, Suansha ren, Caoguoren, Yizhiren each 2 qian, Houpo, Shenqu, and toasted barley each 3 qian. Grind into powder, form into pills the size of corn, and take with rice drink. For weak spleen and stomach, take with rice soup; for vomiting, take with ginger decoction; for food accumulation, take with hawthorn decoction; for abdominal pain, take with fennel decoction; for swelling, take with radish decoction; for cold diarrhea, take with ginger and date decoction.[41p]

　　肥儿丸 【《育婴家秘》】 　小儿脾胃素弱，食少而瘦，或素强健，偶因伤食成积而瘦，或因火病之后而瘦者，宜服之。　　人参　白朮各二钱　陈皮　茯苓各钱半　甘草炙　木香　缩砂仁　青皮　神曲炒　使君子肉各一钱　山药　莲肉去心，各二钱　桔梗一钱　共为细末，荷叶浸汤，煮粳米粉为丸，米饮下。此参苓白朮散加减，以治疳病将成之圣药也。腹中有癖者，加三棱、莪朮各煨，九肋鳖甲醋炙各一钱半。有热者，加北柴胡二钱，黄芩、黄连、芦荟，干烧存性，各一钱半。瘦太甚者，加当归、川芎各二钱。泄泻者，加肉豆蔻面包煨、诃子肉各一钱。疳瘦食少者，去麦芽、神曲。[42p]

Fat Child Pill

【From "Secrets of Child Rearing"】

If a child has a weak spleen and stomach, eats little and is thin, or is generally strong but becomes thin due to food injury, or becomes thin after a fiery illness, it is advisable to take this remedy.

Ingredients:

  • Ginseng: 6g
  • Atractylodes: 6g
  • Dried tangerine peel: 4.5g
  • Poria: 4.5g
  • Honey-fried licorice: 4g
  • Wood fragrance: 4g
  • Shrinking cardamom: 4g
  • Green peel: 4g
  • Fried shenqu (a fermented dough): 4g
  • Fructus forsythiae: 4g
  • Chinese yam: 6g
  • Lotus seeds (remove the heart): 6g
  • Platycodon: 4g

Grind into a fine powder. Soak in lotus leaf soup, cook glutinous rice flour to form pills, and take with rice drink. This is a modified version of the Shenling Baizhu San, to treat malnutrition in children.

If there are masses in the abdomen, add 4.5g each of xingren and evodia, and boil with 6g of the vinegar-fried shell of a soft-shelled turtle.

For heat conditions, add 6g of Bupleurum, 4.5g each of Scutellaria, Coptis, and Aloe vera, each dry-fried until they retain their properties.

For excessive thinness, add 6g each of Angelica and Chuanxiong.

For diarrhea, add 4g each of roasted nutmeg and haritaki fruit.

For malnutrition with little appetite, remove malt and shenqu.[42p]

　　木香丸 【《婴童百问》，下同】 　治吐乳泻乳，其气酸臭，由啼叫不已，以乳与儿，停滞不化，是为乳积。肚硬热渴吐泻，由饮食无度，过饱即睡，是为食积。腹痛啼叫，利如蟹渤，由触忤其气，荣卫不和，淹延日久，是为气积。疟后肚内结癖成块。　　木香　蓬朮　砂仁　青皮去穰　朱砂研细　代赭石　大丁香各一钱　巴豆去油二钱　　右为细末和匀，飞白面糊和丸麻子大，每服二三丸，乳伤乳汁下，食伤米饮下。[43p]

Muxiang Pill

Used to treat vomiting and diarrhea in infants, where the air is sour and foul due to persistent crying, leading to stagnant and undigested milk, known as milk accumulation. A hard belly, heat, thirst, vomiting, and diarrhea resulting from excessive eating and drinking, sleeping right after overeating, known as food accumulation. Abdominal pain accompanied by crying, with a watery diarrhea resembling crabs, resulting from disturbance to the body's energy due to prolonged disharmony of the protective and nutritive Qi, known as Qi accumulation. After a bout of malaria, there may be lumps formed in the abdomen.

Ingredients:

  • Muxiang (costus root)
  • Pengzhu (wormwood)
  • Sharen (amomum)
  • Qingpi (green tangerine peel) without pith
  • Ground fine cinnabar
  • Daizhashi (reddish clay)
  • Daxiang (large cloves)
  • Erbaduo (refined croton seed) without oil

Each ingredient measures one qian, except for Erbaduo, which is two qian. Mix these into a fine powder, form into pills the size of sesame seeds, and take two to three pills each time. These will help eliminate injured milk or food-related ailments.[43p]

　　取癖丸　治小儿癖块大痛，用之如应。　　甘遂　芫花俱微炒　黑牵牛半炒半生取末　辣桂　蓬朮　青皮去穰　木香　桃仁炒　五灵脂各二钱　巴豆去油，一钱　　右为末，研和十分细嫩，飞白面糊丸麻子大，每服一二丸，姜蜜煎汤灌下，泄后冷粥补，仍和胃。
　　挨癖丸　治乳癖谷症，腹中块痛。
　　青皮　木香　代赭石火煅酢淬，研极细末　蓬朮　生地黄各三钱　巴豆压去油，一钱　　右为细末，酢面糊丸麻子大，每服二丸，食后姜汤下。
　　槟榔丸　治小儿伤食得之，痛刺胁肋，心胸烦闷，饮食不下，吐逆恶心，久不医治，渐成痞癖。　　青皮五钱，去穰，巴豆三十粒去壳同炒，去巴豆　陈米半合，炒法亦用巴豆，同青皮　槟榔五钱　木香面裹煨，三钱　　右为细末，蒸饼丸如黍米大，用米饮，食前服。丸数多少，量儿大小虚实加减。[44p]

Ingredients include:

  • Green Peel
  • Mu Xiang

  • Mugwort
  • Sheng Di Huang, each three qian

    Mix into a fine powder, roll into pills the size of a sesame seed. Take two pills after meals with ginger soup.

Bing Lang Wan: For treating children injured by food, leading to pain in the side and ribs, anxiety in the chest, inability to eat, vomiting, nausea, and, if untreated, developing into phlegm masses. Ingredients include:

  • Ba Dou, thirty seeds, shelled and roasted together, and avoid Ba Dou
  • Chen Mi, half a he, also roasted in the same manner as Ba Dou
  • Bing Lang, five qian

    Mix into a fine powder, steam into pills the size of millet, and take with rice drink before meals. The number of pills should be adjusted according to the child's size and condition.[44p]

North Bupleurum Powder: Treats children who have issues arising from injury to the blood, characterized by chest oppression, pain radiating to the lower abdomen, occasional attacking heart and chest sensations, which gradually lead to accumulations. The ingredients are: ginseng, North bupleurum, wood fragrance, bitter orange peel, Beijing sparganium, and betel nut, each three qian. Grind them into a fine powder, decoct with aged tangerine peel, and take on an empty stomach.

Brown Pill: Treats children suffering from injury to qi, presenting with abdominal distension, enlarged belly, flank pain, pale complexion, emaciation, fatigue, and weakness. If left untreated for a long time, it can lead to lumps. The ingredients include: aged tangerine peel, green tangerine peel, sparganium, roasted radish seeds, and curcuma, each five qian; wood fragrance and pepper, one qian each. Grind the charred black ingredients into a fine powder, then make into pills the size of millet grains, with three slices of fresh ginger, soaked in decoction to wash down two to thirty pills.

Seven Fragrance Pill: Treats children suffering from accumulation due to injury, with symptoms resembling intestinal dysentery—excessive and unformed bowel movements, resembling dysentery but not quite, leading to formed masses. The ingredients are: clove, wood fragrance, and star anise, each one and a half qian; bitter orange peel, sparganium, green tangerine peel, and curcuma, along with seven fried red beans (remove the beans), each one qian. Grind into a fine powder, make into pills the size of millet grains, using thirty pills with rice drink on an empty stomach.[45p]

　　圣惠甘遂破结散　治小儿心胸痞结，蕴聚痰水，虽服汤药，暂利而滞实不去，心下坚胀，按之辄啼，内有伏热所结。　　甘遂面裹煨令黄色，二钱半　青皮　黄芩　川大黄煨，各半两　　右为粗末，每服一钱，水一盏，煎至六分，去滓温和服，量大小加减，得通利即止，后以冷粥补之。
　　进食丸　治乳食不消，心腹胀满，壮热喘粗，呕吐痰逆，腹鸣泄泻，米谷不化；或下痢赤白，腹痛后重；及食症乳癖，痃气痞结，并皆治之。小儿胸膈热实，腹内有留饮，致令荣卫痞塞，脏腑之气不得宣通，其病腹内气结，胀满或壮热，凡有此疾，当疏利大便，破结散气，宜常服之。　　巴豆霜一钱　朱砂飞，五钱　枳壳炒，五钱　当归泔浸炒　代赭石煅酢淬七次，各三钱　木香五钱　麝少许　　右为末，面糊为丸如麻子大，一岁儿一丸，米饮下，更量虚实加减，食后服。治食积发热，羸瘦肚大，青筋疳积，肚疼哺露。[46p]

Sheng Hui's Gan Sui for Breaking Masses

This remedy treats children suffering from chest and abdominal blockages, accumulation of phlegm and water. Even with the consumption of decoctions, the condition may temporarily improve but the masses remain, leading to a hard and bloated feeling beneath the heart. If pressed, the child cries, indicating underlying heat causing the blockage.

Take Gan Sui, processed to a yellow color, two and a half qian; combined with an equal amount of Qing Pi, Huang Qin, and Chuan Da Huang, each half a liang. Grind these into a coarse powder. Administer one qian with a bowl of water, decoct until reduced to two-thirds, discard the residue, and serve warm. Adjust the dosage according to the child's size; stop once bowel movement is achieved, and afterwards provide a cold porridge as nourishment.

Jin Shi Wan for Food Accumulation

This remedy treats undigested dairy food, resulting in bloating of the heart and abdomen, severe heat, wheezing, vomiting of phlegm, rumbling intestines, and diarrhea, especially with undigested grains. It also addresses conditions like dysentery with red and white stools, abdominal pain with a heavy feeling afterward, and issues like milk swellings and congested qi.

When there is heat and fullness in a child’s chest, retention of fluids in the abdomen leads to stagnation of the protective and nutritive qi, causing the gas in the abdomen to accumulate, resulting in bloating or excessive heat. For such conditions, one should clear and facilitate bowel movements regularly and break up accumulated qi.

The ingredients include:

  • Ba Dou Shuang, one qian
  • Zhu Sha, five qian
  • Zhi Ke, roasted, five qian
  • Dong Gui, immersed and roasted, with Dai Zhe Shi, calcined with vinegar seven times, three qian each
  • Mu Xiang, five qian
  • A little Musk

These should be ground into powder, mixed into paste, and formed into pills the size of sesame seeds. For a one-year-old, administer one pill with rice drink, adjusting the dosage based on their condition. Take after meals. This remedy treats heat from food accumulation, emaciation with a distended belly, and causes abdominal pain upon nursing.[46p]

　　消积丸　治乳食伤积，心腹胀满，气粗壮热，或泻或呕。　　丁香二十粒　砂仁二十粒　使君子五个　乌梅三个　　右为末，烂饭丸麻子大，加巴豆三粒，去尽油同丸，每服三丸，陈皮汤下。
　　白饼子　治小儿夹食伤寒，其证发热呕吐，亦有肚疼者，嗳气辨得分晓。先用此药，一服推下食积，却用平和药发散调治，如惺惺散、加减参苏饮，皆可服，却不可服冷药。　　滑石　天南星　半夏各一钱　轻粉五分　巴豆二十四粒，去皮膜，用水一升，煮干研细如泥　　右三味，捣罗为末，入巴豆霜，次入轻粉，又研匀，却入余药末，令匀，糯米饮丸如菉豆大，量小儿壮瘦虚实用药。三岁已下每服三丸至五丸，紫苏汤空心下。忌热物。若三五岁儿壮实者，不以此拘，加至三十丸，以利为度。一方加白附子一钱。[47p]

Xiaoji Pill: Treats accumulation from dairy and food injury, causing bloating in the heart and abdomen, rough and strong heat, possibly leading to diarrhea or vomiting.

  • 20 sand seeds
  • 5 Quisqualis

White Bunzi: Treats childhood food accumulation and cold, presenting with fever and vomiting, and sometimes abdominal pain, with belching differentiating symptoms. First, use this medication to push down food accumulation, then apply gentle and balancing medicine for adjustment, such as Xingxing Powder or modified Shen Su Decoction, all can be utilized, but avoid cold medicines.

Ingredients:

  • 1 qian of talc
  • 1 qian of Tian Nanxing
  • 1 qian of ban xia
  • 0.5 qian of light powder
  • 24 beans of croton, peeled, boiled in 1 sheng of water until dry, ground into a paste.

Mix the three ingredients, add croton powder, then light powder, and grind evenly. Finally, add the remaining powdered medicines and mix thoroughly. Form into pills the size of mung beans. Adjust the amount based on the child’s build: for children under 3 years old, take 3 to 5 pills, with perilla leaf soup on an empty stomach. Avoid hot foods. For strong and healthy children aged 3 to 5, do not restrict; increase to 30 pills for effect. One variant adds 1 qian of white fuling.[47p]
