Shao Yao Gan Cao Tang treats exogenous febrile illness with a floating pulse, spontaneous sweating, frequent and troublesome urination, mild aversion to cold, and severe pain or cramping in the abdomen and sides.

Guanyin powder
Stone lotus meat, ginseng, and fried shenqu, each three qian; white poria two qian; fried licorice, wood incense, fried astragalus, and fried white hyacinth bean (peeled) each one qian. Right powder, each dose two qian, one bowl of water, one date, and three leaves of fragrant herb decocted; to be taken warm on an empty stomach.

Silver-white powder, for stopping vomiting and diarrhea, strengthening stomach qi, treating green feces. Glutinous rice and hyacinth bean each two liang; fragrant herb and fried white poria two liang; clove two qian; fried licorice three qian. Right as powder, to be mixed with purple perilla rice drink. Add Tianma, sand ginger, and white poria. For quickening the spleen and restoring color, add fried white atractylodes, whole scorpion, wood incense, stone lotus, and ginger decocted.

Wood incense and betel nut pill, to unblock the three jiao, ease the chest and diaphragm, disperse phlegm and promote fluid, and moisten the large intestine. (Wood fragrant) peach kernels, fried soapwort with vinegar, banxia shenqu, fried bitter orange peel, green skin, almond flour fried, wood incense not exposed to fire, and betel nut each one qian. Right as fine powder, separately use four liang of soapwort, with one bowl of paste, knead and cook into a thick syrup, then add a little熟蜜 (cooked honey), forming pills the size of a wutong seed. Each dose ten pills; for children, form into the size of a mung bean, taken after meals with ginger soup.[49p]

　　神芎丸　治风热壅滞，头目昏眩，口舌生疮，牙齿疳蚀；或遍身疮疥，咬牙，惊惕，怔忡，烦躁多渴；或大小便濇滞；或积热腹满，惊风潮搐，并皆治之。　　生大黄　黄芩各二两　生牵牛头末三两　滑石四两　黄连　薄荷叶　川芎各半两　　右为细末，滴水丸桐子大，每服四五十丸，食后温水下。一方加蒲黄，止血证亦用。
　　是斋推气丸　治三焦痞塞，气不升降，胸膈胀满，大便闭濇，小便赤少。　　大黄　陈皮　槟榔　枳实小者去穰　黄芩　黑牵牛各等分　　右为细末，炼蜜丸如菉豆大，临卧温熟水下二三十丸，量虚实加减。
　　槟榔丸　治小儿疳气腹胀，胸膈痞闷，喘急不安。　　青皮去穰，同巴豆十粒炒，去巴豆　萝卜子　香附子炒　木香各一两　黑牵牛半两，微炒　　右为末，生姜自然汁，煮面糊丸黍米大，每服十丸，米饮下。[50p]

Shen Xiong Pill treats wind-heat obstruction, dizziness, ulcers on the tongue and lips, decayed teeth; or widespread sores and scabs, grinding of teeth, agitation, fright, restlessness, and excessive thirst; or difficulties in urination and defecation; or abdominal fullness due to accumulated heat, convulsions from fright, all of which it can treat.

Ingredients:

  • Raw Da Huang (Rhizoma Rhei) 120g
  • Huang Qin (Radix Scutellariae) 120g
  • Raw Qian Niu Zi (Semen Pharbitidis) powder 180g
  • Hua Shi (Talcum) 240g
  • Huang Lian (Rhizoma Coptidis)
  • Bo He (Folium Menthae)
  • Chuan Xiong (Rhizoma Chuanxiong) each 15g

Grind to a fine powder, form into pills the size of a tung seed, take 40-50 pills with warm water after meals. An option adds Pu Huang (Pollen Typhae), also used for stopping bleeding.

Zhai Tui Qi Pill treats stagnation in the San Jiao, inability to regulate qi, chest fullness, constipation, redness and diminished urination.

Ingredients:

  • Da Huang (Rhizoma Rhei)
  • Chen Pi (Pericarpium Citri Reticulatae)
  • Bing Lang (Semen Arecae)
  • Zhi Shi (Fructus Aurantii) small ones with seeds removed
  • Huang Qin (Radix Scutellariae)
  • Hei Qian Niu (Semen Pharbitidis) each in equal parts

Grind to a fine powder, refine with honey into pills the size of a mung bean, take 20-30 pills with warm cooked water before bed, adjust dosage based on condition.

Bing Lang Pill treats children's nutritional disturbances with abdominal bloating, chest oppression, and acute wheezing.

Ingredients:

  • Qing Pi (Pericarpium Citri Viride) without seeds
  • Nine fried Ba Dou (Semen Crotonis), remove Ba Dou
  • Luo Bo Zi (Semen Raphani)
  • Xiang Fu Zi (Rhizoma Cyperi)
  • Mu Xiang (Radix Aucklandiae) each 30g
  • Hei Qian Niu (Semen Pharbitidis) 15g, slightly fried

Grind to a powder, mix with fresh ginger juice to cook into a dough, form into pills the size of millet, take 10 pills with rice drink.[50p]

　　消食丸　常服宽中快气，消乳食，正颜色。　　缩砂　陈皮　三棱　蓬朮　神曲炒　麦芽炒　香附泔浸一宿炒　枳壳　槟榔　乌梅各五钱　丁香二钱五分　　右为末，面糊丸如菉豆大，食后紫苏汤送下二三十丸。
　　快膈消食丸　治小儿宿食停滞，腹胀疼痛。　　三棱煨　蓬莪朮煨　拣缩砂去壳　橘皮去白　神曲炒　麦芽炒，各五钱　香附子炒，一钱　　右为细末，蒸饼丸如黍米大，生姜煎汤或白汤，或将饼子磨，食远服。一方加制枳壳。
　　香棱丸　治小儿积气发热，肚腹膨胀，肢体瘦弱，饮食不滋肌肤。　　木香　丁香　槟榔去脐　枳壳炒　甘松　使君子去壳　神曲炒　麦芽炒，各二钱半　三棱煨　莪朮　青皮　陈皮　香附炒，各五钱　胡黄连一钱　　右为细末，蒸饼丸如黍米大，用米饮，食远服。
　　五珍丸　治酒食积通用。
　　青皮　干姜烧存性　蓬朮　五灵脂各一两　巴豆去半油一钱　　右为末，粳米饭丸麻子大，每服三五丸，米汤下。[51p]

Digestive Pills: Regular consumption helps to soothe the stomach, ease gas, alleviate food stagnation, and improve complexion. Ingredients: Sandwort, dried tangerine peel, sparganium, fried fermented rice, roasted malt, fried cyperus (soaked overnight), bitter orange peel, betel nut, black plum, each five qian; cloves two qian and five fen. Grind into powder, form into pills the size of a mung bean, take two to thirty pills after meals with perilla broth.

Fast-Gong Digestive Pills: Treats children’s food stagnation, abdominal distension, and pain. Ingredients: Three-angled fruit (stewed), sparganium and aged cyperus (stewed), select the sandwort and remove the shells, remove the white part of tangerine peel, fried fermented rice, roasted malt, each five qian; fried cyperus one qian. Grind into fine powder, form into pills the size of millet, take with ginger decoction or clear broth, or ground into a paste, consumed from a distance. One recipe adds prepared bitter orange peel.

Fragrant Angle Pills: Treats children with accumulated gas, fever, abdominal swelling, frail limbs, and poor appetite. Ingredients: Wood fragrance, cloves, betel nut (remove navel), roasted bitter orange peel, licorice, campanumoea (remove shell), fried fermented rice, roasted malt, each two qian and five fen; three-angled fruit (stewed), aged cyperus, green peel, dried tangerine peel, fried cyperus, each five qian; and huanglian one qian. Grind into fine powder, form into pills the size of millet, take with rice drink, consumed from a distance.

Five Treasures Pills: Treats food and alcohol accumulation, commonly used. Ingredients: Green peel, dried ginger (roasted), cyperus, five spirit resin each one liang; half a qian of castor bean (remove half oil). Grind into powder, form into pills the size of millet, take three to five pills with rice soup.[51p]

小儿食癖门

　　　　方

　　理中清热汤 【《明医杂着》】 　治小儿食积郁热，发于肌表，潮热往来。主理中，清阳明之热。　　白朮炒　山渣　白芍药炒各一钱　黄连炒　枳实麸炒　川芎　香附米炒　升麻各七分　葛根一钱二分　甘草　炙草各三分　　右用姜水煎服。若食积去后，潮热未除，减山楂、枳实、香附、川芎，加人参、黄芪、陈皮各五分，再加白朮二三分。有痰加半夏六分。薛己曰：按前证若食积去而热不退，用五味异功散以补胃气。若作呕少食，用四君子加藿香、半夏以安中气。若泄泻不食，宜用六君子汤加升麻、柴胡以升补脾气。若久泻不已，宜用补中益气汤以升补阳气。若虚寒加炮姜、木香；如不应，佐以四神丸以补脾肾。若体瘦潮热，口渴，大便不调，宜用肥儿丸以消疳积。若不分脾气虚实，有无食积，概用克伐消导寒凉清热之剂，复伤脾胃生气，反为难治之证。[52p]

Title: Complete Compilation of Ancient and Modern Books, Volume 442 - Children's Dietary Disorders

Recipe

Liqing Heat-clearing Decoction [from "Miscellaneous Writings of Ming Physicians"]

Used for treating children's food accumulation with stagnation heat, manifesting on the skin with alternating fever. It primarily regulates the interior and clears the heat of the yangming.

Ingredients:

  • Fried Atractylodes - 1 qian
  • Hawthorn - 1 qian
  • Fried White Peony - 1 qian
  • Fried Coptis - 7 fen
  • Fried Bitter Orange - 7 fen
  • Chuanxiong - 7 fen
  • Fried Cyperus - 7 fen
  • Shengma - 7 fen
  • Pueraria - 1 qian 2 fen
  • Honey-fried Licorice - 3 fen
  • Licorice - 3 fen

Prepare by decocting with ginger water. If the food accumulation is resolved but the alternating fever persists, reduce Hawthorn, Bitter Orange, Cyperus, and Chuanxiong, and add 5 fen each of Ginseng, Astragalus, and Dried Tangerine Peel, along with an additional 2-3 fen of Atractylodes. If there is phlegm, add 6 fen of Pinellia.

Xue Ji states: If the symptoms indicate that the food accumulation is resolved but the heat does not recede, use Wuwei Yigong Powder to replenish stomach qi. If there are symptoms of vomiting and reduced appetite, use Si Junzi Decoction with Agastache and Pinellia to stabilize the qi in the stomach. If diarrhea occurs and lacks appetite, it’s advisable to use Liu Junzi Decoction with Shengma and Chaihu to tonify spleen qi. If diarrhea persists for a long time, use Buzhong Yiqi Decoction to boost yang qi.

For deficiencies and coldness, add roasted Ginger and Muxiang; if ineffective, assist with Sishen Pill to tonify spleen and kidney. If the body is thin with alternating fever, thirst, and irregular bowel movements, use Fei’er Pill to resolve dietary accumulation.

If the distinction between spleen qi deficiency and food accumulation is unclear, it is advisable to avoid any measures that cold or clear heat, as they may further harm the spleen and stomach, leading to challenging conditions to treat.[52p]

　　人参安胃散 【《保婴撮要》，下同】 　治脾胃虚弱，伤热乳食，呕吐泻痢。　　人参一钱　黄芪二钱　生甘草　炙草各五分　白芍药酒炒，七分　白茯苓四分　陈皮三分　黄连炒，二分　　右为末，每服二钱，水煎。薛己曰：愚按东垣云：益黄散内有丁香、青皮之辛热，盖为寒水侮土而设也。若因热药巴豆之类，损其脾胃，或因暑热伤乳食而成吐泻，口鼻气热而致慢惊者，宜用前方。
　　益黄散　治脾虚吐泻不食，米谷不化，困倦力少，滑肠夜起，并疳虚盗汗，涎流口角。　　陈皮一两　丁香二钱　诃子炮去皮　青皮　甘草炙，各半两　　右为末，每服一钱，水煎服。薛己曰：愚按前证，若脾土虚寒，或寒水侮土而呕吐泄泻，手足并冷，或痰涎上涌，睡而露睛，不思乳食，宜用此方。若因脾土虚弱吐泻者，用六君子汤加柴胡；如不应，或手足俱冷，属虚寒也，更加木香、炮姜。若因乳母脾虚肝侮，必治以前药。[53p]

Ginseng Stomach Tranquil Powder

This formula is used to treat weakness of the spleen and stomach, damage from excessive heat in milk and food, vomiting and diarrhea.

Ingredients:

  • Ginseng: 1 qian
  • Astragalus: 2 qian
  • Raw licorice: 0.5 qian
  • Honey-fried licorice: 0.5 qian
  • White peony root (stir-fried in wine): 0.7 qian
  • White poria: 0.4 qian
  • Aged orange peel: 0.3 qian
  • Stir-fried coptis: 0.2 qian

Grind all ingredients into a powder. Dose: 2 qian each time, decocted in water.

Xue Ji says: According to Dongyuan, the Yi Huang Powder includes the spicy heat of clove and green tangerine peel, which is meant to counteract cold water's invasion of earth. If heat-damaging medicines like cassia seed cause harm to the spleen and stomach, or if summer heat injures the intake of milk and food leading to vomiting and diarrhea with a hot wind in the mouth and nose causing prolonged fright, this formula should be used.

Yi Huang Powder

This formula treats spleen deficiency leading to vomiting, diarrhea, and loss of appetite, with poor digestion of grains, fatigue, low energy, night-time bowel movements, wasting with night sweats, and drooling at the corners of the mouth.

Ingredients:

  • Aged orange peel: 1 liang
  • Clove: 2 qian
  • Haritaki (roasted and peeled): 0.5 liang
  • Green tangerine peel: 0.5 liang
  • Licorice (honey-fried): 0.5 liang

Grind all ingredients into a powder. Dose: 1 qian each time, decocted in water.

Xue Ji says: In previous cases, if the spleen is deficient and cold or if cold water overcomes earth leading to vomiting and diarrhea, or if hands and feet are cold, or if phlegm rises with eyes half-open during sleep and there is a lack of desire for milk and food, this formula should be used. If the vomiting and diarrhea are due to spleen deficiency, use Six Gentleman Decoction with Chai Hu. If there is no response, or if the hands and feet are cold, it indicates true cold, and one should add wood fragrance and roasted ginger. If the issue arises from a wet nurse’s spleen deficiency and liver insult, one must treat with the previous formulas.[53p]

若乳母郁怒，致儿患前证，母服加味归脾汤。王肯堂曰：东垣云：阎孝忠编集钱氏方，以益黄散补土。又言：风旺必克脾土，当先实其脾。昧者不审脾中寒热，一例用补脾药；又不审药中有丁香、青皮辛热，大泻肺金，脾虚之证，岂可反泻其子？为寒水反来侮土，中寒呕吐，腹痛，泻痢青白，口鼻中气冷，益黄散神治之药也。如因服热药巴豆之类过剂，损其脾胃，或因暑天伤热积热，损其脾胃，而成吐泻，口鼻中气热而成慢惊者，不可服之，故立人参安胃散。[54p]

If the wet nurse is extremely angry, it can lead to the child suffering from symptoms of illness. The mother should take a modified Gui Pi decoction. Wang Kentang said: Dongyuan states that Yan Xiaozhong compiled the Qian family's prescriptions to enhance Huang San for nourishing the earth. He also mentioned that when wind is strong, it must overcome the spleen's earth, so one must first strengthen the spleen. Those in ignorance do not discern the cold and heat within the spleen, treating all cases uniformly with spleen-nourishing medicines; they also fail to recognize that medicines containing cloves and citrus peels are pungent and warm, severely draining the lung's metal. How can one reverse the outflow in a case of spleen deficiency? It turns the cold water against the earth, causing cold-related vomiting, abdominal pain, greenish or white diarrhea, and a cold sensation in the mouth and nose. Huang San is the appropriate remedy for this condition. If, however, the illness arises from taking excessive hot medicines like ba dou, which harm the spleen and stomach, or if it is due to the heat accumulated during hot weather, leading to vomiting and diarrhea, with a hot sensation in the mouth and nose resulting in a state of chronic fright, it should not be used. Therefore, Ren Shen An Wei San should be prescribed.[54p]

　　钱氏泻黄散　一名泻脾散。治脾热吐舌。　　藿香叶　甘草各七钱五分　山栀仁一两　石膏五钱　防风二两　　右用蜜酒微炒为末，每服一二钱，水煎。薛己曰：愚按前证，若作渴饮冷，卧不露睛，手足热甚，或遍身发黄，属胃经实热，宜用泻黄散。若作渴饮汤，卧而露睛，手足并冷，属胃经虚热，宜用异功散。若面青搐搦，乳食少思，肝乘脾也，用秘旨补脾汤。若面赤惊悸，身热昏睡，心乘脾也，用秘旨安神丸。若面白喘嗽，肢体倦怠，肺乘脾也，用补中益气汤。若唇黑泄泻，手足指冷，肾乘脾也，用益黄散。病后津液不足，口干作渴，宜用七味白朮散。若乳母膏粱厚味，七情郁火所致，当审其因而治其母。[55p]

Qian's Xiehuang Powder, also known as Xiepisan, treats spleen heat and tongue vomiting.

Ingredients:

  • 7.5 grams of Huoxiang leaves
  • 7.5 grams of Licorice
  • 30 grams of Mountain Gardenia seeds
  • 25 grams of Gypsum
  • 40 grams of Fangfeng

Preparation: Grind into a fine powder after lightly frying with honey wine. The dosage is one to two grams, to be decocted in water.

Xue Ji states: Based on the symptoms, if there is thirst with a preference for cold drinks, sleeping with eyes closed, and hands and feet feeling very hot, or if there is general yellowing of the body, it belongs to excess heat in the stomach channel, and Xiehuang Powder is appropriate. If there is thirst with a preference for soup, sleeping with eyes open, and hands and feet cold, it indicates a deficiency of heat in the stomach channel, appropriate for Yi Gong Powder. If the face is pale and the person frequently craves milk food, this suggests liver overacting on the spleen, and the remedy is the Secret Formula to Tonify the Spleen Decoction. If there is a red face with anxiety, body heat, and drowsiness, it indicates heart overacting on the spleen, appropriate for the Secret Formula to Calm the Spirit Pill. If the face is pale with wheezing, fatigue in the limbs, this indicates lung overacting on the spleen, appropriate for the Restore the Middle and Augment Qi Decoction. If there is blackened lips with diarrhea, and cold in the hands and feet, this indicates kidney overacting on the spleen, suitable for the Benefit Yellow Powder. After illness, if there is insufficient body fluids, dry mouth, and thirst, the Seven Flavor Bai Zhu Powder is recommended. If a nursing mother consumes rich foods that cause internal heat from emotional distress, her condition should be examined and treated.[55p]

　　平胃散 【《证治准绳》，下同】 　治脾胃不和，不思饮食，心腹胁肋胀满刺痛，口苦无味，胸满短气，呕哕恶心，嗳气吞酸，面黄肌瘦，嗜卧体痛，霍乱吐泻等证。　　厚朴姜汁制，五两　陈皮　甘草炙，各一两　苍朮米泔浸焙，八两　　右为末，每服二钱，姜枣水煎，沸汤点服亦可。常服调气暖胃，化宿食，消痰饮，辟四时不正之气。愚按前证，若乳食停滞，嗳腐吞酸，呕吐恶心者，宜服是方。若饮食既消，脾胃虚弱，呕吐恶心者，则宜四君子汤。
　　调中丸　治脾胃虚寒。
　　白朮　人参　甘草炒，各五分
　　右加八味地黄丸，即六味地黄丸加肉桂、附子各一两，治禀赋命门火衰，不能生土，以致脾土虚寒，或饮食少思，及食而不化，腹脐疼痛，多旋溺等证。《内经》谓益火之源以消阴翳，正此药也。
　　人参散　治脾风多困。[56p]

Pingwei Powder

Treats disharmony of the spleen and stomach, lack of appetite, distension and stabbing pain in the chest and sides, bitter taste with no flavor, fullness in the chest and shortness of breath, nausea and vomiting, belching with sourness, pale complexion and emaciation, lethargy and body pain, as well as symptoms of cholera like vomiting and diarrhea.

Ingredients:

  • 250 grams of huangqi (thick fragrant)
  • 50 grams each of dried tangerine peel and honey-fried licorice
  • 400 grams of caoguo (Atractylodes), soaked and roasted

Grind these into a powder. For each dose, take 6 grams, decoct with ginger and jujube water, or it can also be taken with boiled soup. Regular use adjusts qi, warms the stomach, transforms stagnant food, resolves phlegm and excess fluids, and expels improper seasonal influences. If symptoms include stagnation from dairy, sour regurgitation, and nausea, this remedy is advised. However, if digestion is already diminished, and the spleen and stomach are weak with nausea, then the Four Gentlemen Decoction should be used.

Tiaozhong Pills

Treats coldness of the spleen and stomach.

Ingredients:

  • 15 grams each of white atractylodes, ginseng, and honey-fried licorice

Additionally, use Bawei Dihuang Pills, which are Liuwei Dihuang Pills plus 30 grams each of cinnamon and aconite, to treat deficiency of the kidney fire which fails to nourish the spleen, leading to coldness of the spleen earth, or lack of appetite, food not being digested, abdominal pain around the navel, and frequent urination, among other symptoms. The Inner Canon states that by benefiting the source of fire one can disperse shadowy yin, and this formula serves that purpose.

Ginseng Powder

Treats excessive wind in the spleen leading to consternation.[56p]

　　南星切片，用浆水姜汁煮存性，一两　人参　冬瓜仁各半两　　右为细末，每服一钱，水半盏，煎二三分，温服。
　　藿香散　理虚化痰，及治脾胃不和，饮食少进，正气除邪。　　人参　半夏汤煮透滤，銼片焙干　赤茯苓　炙草各一两　苍朮米泔浸一宿，滤銼炒黄，二两　陈皮　藿香各七钱五分　厚朴制，一两半　　右件(口父)咀，每服二钱，水一盏，姜二片，枣一枚，煎七分，空心温服。或入烧盐同煎。
　　四君子散　治小儿脾胃虚弱，饮食少进。　　人参　白朮　茯苓　甘草各等分
　　右为末，每服一钱，盐汤点服。一方加陈皮、缩砂。
　　参苓白朮散　主脾胃虚弱，饮食不进，多困少气，中满痞结，噫呕吐逆，此药不寒不热，性味和平，常服调脾悦色，顺正去邪。　　人参　白茯苓　粉草　白朮　白扁豆炒去壳　干山药　缩砂仁　薏苡仁　桔梗銼炒，各一两　莲子肉　　右銼焙为末，每服半钱至一钱，用枣汤空心调服，或温米汤亦可。[57p]

Sliced南星, boiled with ginger juice and water, each weighing one tael; half a tael each of ginseng and winter melon seeds. Grind to a fine powder. Take one qian with half a tea cup of water, simmer for two to three minutes, and take warm.

Huangqi Powder regulates deficiency and resolves phlegm, treating disharmony of spleen and stomach, with reduced appetite. Ginseng and Banxia are boiled, filtered, and dried; red poria and roasted licorice each weigh one tael. Cangzhu, soaked overnight in rice water, filtered, and roasted until yellow, weighs two taels. Dried tangerine peel and Huangqi each weigh seven and a half qian. Weight of the ingredients totals one and a half taels. Each dose is two qian, taken with one cup of water, two slices of ginger, and one date, simmered for seven minutes, and taken warm on an empty stomach. Alternatively, it can be simmered with burnt salt.

Four Gentlemen Powder treats weakened spleen and stomach in children with reduced appetite. Ginseng, white atractylodes, poria, and licorice are used in equal parts. Grind into powder. Each dose is one qian, taken with salted water. One variation adds tangerine peel and sand tamarind.

Ginseng and Poria Atractylodes Powder addresses weakness of the spleen and stomach, reduced appetite, fatigue, feelings of fullness, and nausea or vomiting. This medicine is neither cold nor hot, has a neutral property, and improves spleen and complexion with regular use, dispelling evils. Ingredients include ginseng, white poria, powdered licorice, white atractylodes, shelled white adzuki beans, dried yam, sand tamarind, coix seeds, and roasted platycodon, each weighing one tael. The lotus seed flesh is ground and roasted into powder. Each dose is half to one qian, taken with date tea on an empty stomach, or warm rice water is also acceptable.[57p]

　　健脾饮　健脾养胃，理呕吐，治泻利，及诸病后气色虚弱，有痰恶心，腹中微痛，饮食减，精神慢，宜服之。　　厚朴銼，姜汁浸一宿，炒干，入醇酢焠透仍炒之　人参各一两　白茯　肉蔻　半夏汤煮透銼焙　益智　香附　良姜壁土炒　诃子肉各二钱　炙草五钱　　右銼，每服二钱，水一盏，姜二片，枣一枚，煎七分，无时服。
　　茅先主匀气散
　　桔梗五两　炙草二两　白姜一分　砂仁　陈橘皮　茴香洗，各一两　　右为末，半钱或一钱，霜木瓜煎汤调服，紫苏盐汤亦得。《宝童》多厚朴、苍朮、良姜、肉桂、乌梅，名养脾汤。

Jianpi Decoction: Strengthens the spleen and nourishes the stomach, regulates vomiting, treats diarrhea, and addresses various post-illness conditions with weak energy and complexion, phlegm and nausea, slight abdominal pain, reduced appetite, and lethargy. It is advisable to take this.

Ingredients:

  • Huangbo (magnolia bark)
  • Ginger juice (soaked overnight, then stir-fried until dry, and further cooked with vinegar)
  • Ginseng (1 liang)
  • Bai Fu Ling (white poria)
  • Nutmeg
  • Ban Xia (pinellia, boiled and roasted)
  • Yi Zhi Ren
  • Xiang Fu (cyperus)
  • Liang Jiang (galanga)
  • Bi Tu (wall soil)
  • He Zi (terminalia fruit, 2 qian each)
  • Zhi Cao (honey fried licorice, 5 qian)

For each dose, grind to a powder, take 2 qian with 1 cup of water, 2 slices of ginger, and 1 jujube; decoct to 70% and take at any time.

Mao Xian Zhu Yin Qi San:

  • Jie Geng (platycodon, 5 liang)

  • Bai Jiang (white ginger, 1 fen)
  • Sha Ren (cardamom)
  • Chen Ju Pi (dried orange peel)

Grind to a powder, take ½ qian or 1 qian, decoct with frost melon or with purple perilla salt soup. "Bao Tong" includes more Huangbo, Cang Zhu, Liang Jiang, cinnamon, and black plum, and is called the Nourishing Spleen Decoction.

Xing Pi Soup: Regulates various ailments.

  • Mu Xiang (saussurea)

  • Bai Fu Ling

Jianpi San: Treats children's stomach Qi.
Ingredients:
White poria (1 tael), ginseng (1 tael), magnolia bark (3 taels, dry-fried with ginger juice), fragrant angelica (4 taels, soaked overnight), tangerine peel (5 taels), fragrant cardamom and licorice (each 2 taels).
Preparation: Grind these into a powder. Each dose is 1 qian, decoct with ginger and jujube, adjusted according to the child's size.

Tiaozhong Yinzi: Treats various children's ailments.
Ingredients:
Nutmeg, fragrant angelica (fried), ginseng, aged tangerine peel, fennel, kapok fruit (fried and pitted), roasted licorice, sand ginger (each 0.5 tael), patchouli, cinnamomum bark, betel nut (each 3 qian).
Preparation: Grind into a powder. Each dose is 0.5 or 1 qian, taken with ginger and jujube decoction, adjusted according to the child's size.

Baotong San: Strengthens the spleen and alleviates accumulation, promotes digestion.
Ingredients:
Beijing sparganium, pungent rhizome (wrapped in paper and steamed), wood fruits (each 4 taels), roasted licorice (4.5 taels), aged and fresh tangerine peel (each 2 taels).
Preparation: Grind into a powder. Take 1 qian with soup occasionally. Can also use ginger and jujube decoction.

Shen Zhu San: Treats weakened spleen and stomach after illness, irritability, confusion, frequent fright during sleep, shortness of breath, and agitation. Nourishes the spleen and stomach, aids digestion, calms the Qi and spirit, harmonizes the organs.
Ingredients:
White atractylodes, ginseng, white poria, lotus seed flesh, poppy seeds, white lentils, patchouli, roasted licorice (each equal portions).
Preparation: Grind finely, take about half a small cup, mix with jujube soup, and take on an empty stomach during the noon hour. For Han Dong Guanyin San, use less white atractylodes and poppy seeds, while increasing the amounts of Shenqu, white angelica, wood incense, and astragalus.[59p]

Shenghui Qianhu San: For treating disharmony of the spleen and stomach, manifesting as lack of appetite, vomiting, and chest oppression. Ingredients: Qianhu and Lu Gen each 3 fen; Gui Xin 1 fen; Ren Shen, Bai Zhu, Chi Fu, and Pi Pa Ye (hair removed and roasted) and Zhi Cao, and Hou Po each 5 liang; coarse Luo 1 qian; water 1 zhan; a little ginger. Zhang Huan Ji Xiang Jin: For treating deficiency of the spleen and stomach, lack of appetite, and emaciation. Ingredients: Huo Xiang Ye, Hou Po (processed with ginger), Ding Xiang, Chen Xiang, Mu Xiang each 1 liang; Bai Fu Ling, Bai Dou Kou, Bai Zhu (fried) each 5 liang. Cook slowly in a silver pot until it forms a paste, remove the ginger and dates, and dry in a ventilated shaded area; each piece should be the size of a soap bar, taken with rice drink before nursing.

Tiao Zhong San: For treating children with cold and heat disharmony leading to disharmony of the spleen and stomach. Ingredients: Mu Xiang, Ren Shen, Bai Zhu, Bai Fu Ling, Ding Xiang, Da Fu Pi, Gan Cao, and Qing Ju Pi, all soaked in soup to remove whiteness and roasted dry, each 1 liang. Grind the above items into a fine powder, take 1 qian each time, with a small zhan of water, and 3 slices of fresh ginger. Boil for five minutes, strain, and take warm.[60p]

Yiwai Dan regulates cold and heat, harmonizing the spleen and stomach.
Ingredients:

  • 1 liang of angelica (Danggui), washed and dried
  • 1 liang of muxiang (costus root)
  • 1 liang of bai zhu (white atractylodes)
  • 1 liang of chen xiang (agarwood)
  • 0.5 liang each of bai shaoyao (white peony root), ren shen (ginseng), pung er zhu (pungent atractylodes), and su zhao ren (amomum villosum)
    Crush and sieve the above into a fine powder. Form into small pills the size of millet, with each dosage being 10 to 15 pills. Take with a few drops of musk-infused water, adjusting the dosage according to the child's size.

Ding Xiang Huang Qi San treats weak spleen and stomach in children that cannot eat or drink, leading to a depletion of vitality and resulting in emaciation, frequent diarrhea, and pale complexion.
Ingredients:

  • 1 liang each of ding xiang (clove), miyan huangqi (astragalus root), ren shen (ginseng), bai zhu (white atractylodes), and angelica (Danggui), washed and dried
  • 1 liang of soft, roasted turtle shell ripped from its skirt
  • 0.5 liang each of hu lian (corydalis) and zhi cao (licorice)
    Crush and sieve the above into a fine powder. Each dose is 1 qian (3 grams) mixed with 1 cup of water, adding 2 slices of fresh ginger and 2 jujubes. Boil down to one fifth, strain and take warm before meals.

Bie Jia Tang treats children aged three to seven who cannot eat, vomit, have a fever, diarrhea, or thirst, or have hot hands and feet that sometimes feel cold. A daily dose will restore their appetite.
Ingredients:

  • 1 liang of bie jia (soft-shelled turtle shell)
  • 2.5 qian each of angelica (Danggui), zhi cao (licorice), and sheng ma (cimicifuga)
  • 50 grains of pepper (jiang)
    Chop the herbs, boil in 1 sheng (approximately 1 liter) of water until reduced to 8 portions. After walking six to seven li (about 2-3 km), take another dose, ensuring the body is comfortable and only a slight sweat is produced.[61p]

　　保和丸　治饮食停滞，胸膈痞满，嗳气吞酸，或吐泻腹痛。加白朮一两，即大安丸。　　神曲炒　山楂　半夏　茯苓各一两　陈皮　连翘　萝卜子炒，各五钱　　右为末，粥丸桐子大，每服三十丸，白汤送下。愚按前方行气克滞之剂，若元气无亏，暴停乳食而致斯证者，宜用此消导之。若元气虚弱，而乳食所伤者，必调补胃气为主，而佐以消导。若乳食已消而作呕者，乃胃气被伤，当用异功散补之，不宜仍用前药，重损胃气，用者审之！
　　木香大安丸
　　木香二钱　黄连　陈皮　白朮各三钱　枳实　山楂肉　莱菔子炒　连翘　神曲炒　麦芽炒　砂仁各一钱半　　右为末，神曲糊为丸，陈廪米汤下。
　　消食丸　又名消乳丸。治宿食不消。　　砂仁　陈皮　三棱　神曲　麦芽各半两　香附一两　　右末，曲糊丸如麻子大，食后白汤送下，量儿大小加减。[62p]

Baohawan treats food stagnation, chest fullness, belching with sourness, or vomiting and abdominal pain. Adding one liang of Atractylodes turns it into Da'anwan.

Shenqu Chao, Hawthorn, Pinellia, and Poria each one liang; dried Tangerine Peel, Forsythia, and fried Radish Seed each five qian. Grind these into a powder, make into balls the size of a Tongzi, and take thirty balls with warm water.

The above formula is for regulating qi and overcoming stagnation. If the vital energy is not deficient, but there is sudden stagnation due to dairy and food, this formula should be used to digest and guide. If the vital energy is weak and harmed by dairy and food, it is essential to restore the stomach's qi primarily, supplemented by digestives. If food has been digested but vomiting occurs, it indicates injury to the stomach's qi, and Yigong San should be used instead. The previous medicine should not be used again, as it may further harm the stomach's qi. Users should be cautious!

Muxiang Da'anwan consists of 2 qian of Muxiang, 3 qian each of Huanglian, Chenpi, and Baizhu, 1.5 qian each of Zhi Shi, Hawthorn flesh, fried Lai Fu Zi, Lianqiao, Shenqu Chao, and malt stir-fried with 1.5 qian of Sand Ginger. Grind into a powder, mix with Shenqu paste to form pills, and take with rice porridge.

Xiaoshiwan, also called Xiaoruwan, treats undigested food. It includes half a liang each of Sand Ginger, Chenpi, Sanleng, Shenqu, and malt, with one liang of Xiangfu. Grind into a powder, mix into balls the size of sesame seeds, and take with warm water after meals, adjusting the dosage for children accordingly.[62p]

　　七圣丸
　　三棱　蓬朮　川楝　青皮　陈皮　芫花　杏仁　　右件等分，先用酢浸芫花一宿，炒渐干，次入蓬棱同炒赤色，又入陈楝等再同炒一处，令微焦取出为末，前药如各半两，杏仁亦用半两，汤浸去皮尖双仁不用，研细，入巴豆二十粒，去油和匀，酢糊丸如黍米大，一岁儿常服二丸，临卧温热汤送下，使日间所餐之物，一夜而化，永无疳疾，能使黄瘦子顿作化生儿。今之小儿，可去巴豆，只入杏仁，名七圣丸是也。
　　三棱散　主诸般停滞，疳积发热，泻痢酸馁，水谷不化。常服和脾胃，进饮食，长肌肉，益神气。　　人参七钱半　三棱炮銼　净香附各一两半　青皮　益智仁　陈皮　谷芽　枳壳麸炒　神曲炒　半夏制　莪朮酢煮透滤干銼焙　大黄半生半炮　紫苏各半两　甘草一两二钱　　右碎，每服二钱，水一盏，姜三片，仓米百粒，煎七分，无时温服。气虚者，加白茯苓一两。[63p]

Seven Holy Pills

Take equal parts of the following ingredients: Sanleng, Pungzhu, Chuanlian, Qingpi, Chenpi, Yanhua, and Xingren. First, soak the Yanhua in vinegar overnight, then stir-fry until slightly dry. Next, add the Sanleng and continue to stir-fry until red. Then, mix in the Chuanlian and the others, frying them together until slightly charred, and grind into a fine powder. Use half a tael of each of the aforementioned herbs, and also take half a tael of Xingren, which should be soaked to remove the skin, keeping only the inner seed. Grind it finely and add twenty grains of Ba Dou, removing the oil and mixing well. Form into pills the size of millet. A one-year-old child can take two pills before bedtime, with warm soup to swallow, which helps the food consumed during the day to digest overnight, preventing any kind of malnutrition. It can also help underweight children to become healthy and robust. For modern children, Ba Dou may be omitted, simply using the Xingren; this is called Seven Holy Pills.

Sanleng Powder

This remedy addresses various stagnations, malnutrition leading to fever, diarrhea, and indigestion. It is used regularly to strengthen the spleen and stomach, aiding in the digestion of food and promoting muscle growth and vitality.

Ingredients include:

  • 7.5 qian of Ren Shen
  • 1.5 taels of Sanleng (stir-fried)
  • 1.5 taels of clean Xiangfu
  • Qingpi
  • Yizhiren
  • Chenpi
  • Guya
  • Zhiqiao (lightly stir-fried)
  • Shenchuan (lightly stir-fried)
  • Banxia (processed)
  • E Zhu (cooked in vinegar, filtered, and roasted)
  • 0.5 taels of Dahuang (half raw, half stir-fried)
  • 0.5 taels of Zisuan

Add 1.2 taels of Gan Cao. Grind these ingredients together. For each dose, take two qian with a cup of water, three slices of ginger, and one hundred grains of rice, and boil until reduced to seven parts. This should be taken warm at any time. For those with qi deficiency, add one tael of Bai Fuling.[63p]

　　莪朮丸　和脾益胃，进饮消食，宽膈快气，悦色清神。　　莪朮　三棱　香附各四两，酢浸七日煮焙　槟榔薄銼　生牵牛末各一两，另研　清木香　谷芽洗净焙干　青皮各半两　荜澄茄　丁香　南木香各四钱　　右除槟榔、丁香、木香不过火，及牵牛末，余七味銼焙，仍同槟榔、丁香、木香为末，临入牵牛末和匀，水煮面糊丸菉豆大，每服三十丸至五十丸，无时，用淡姜汤下，温茶温酒皆好。儿小者丸粟米大数粒，下法如前。
　　丁香脾积丸
　　三棱煨去皮毛　莪朮炒　神曲炒，各七钱　青皮　巴豆霜　小茴香炒　陈皮各五钱　丁香　木香各三钱　　右为细末，酢调神曲糊为丸如菉豆大，每服五七丸，生姜汤下。
　　三黄枳朮丸　治伤肉湿面辛辣味厚之物，致填塞闷乱不快。　　枳实麸炒　黄芩各五钱　川黄连酒浸炒　大黄湿纸裹煨　白朮各一两　　右为末，汤浸蒸饼为丸如菉豆大，每服五十丸，白汤下。临时量所伤多少，加减服之。[64p]

E Zhu Pill
Harmonizes the spleen and benefits the stomach, promotes drinking and digestion, alleviates chest fullness and aids in regulating qi, enhancing complexion and spirit.
E Zhu, San Leng, and Xiang Fu, each four taels, soaked in vinegar for seven days, then boiled and dried. Areca nut, finely shaved, and fresh Qian Niu Zi, each one tael, ground separately. Qing Mu Xiang and Gu Ya, washed clean and dried, each half a tael. Bi Cheng Qie, Ding Xiang, and Nan Mu Xiang, each four qian.
Except for areca nut, clove, and wood fragrance, which should not be exposed to fire, and fresh Qian Niu Zi, the remaining seven ingredients are finely ground and blended with areca nut, clove, and wood fragrance. Mix in fresh Qian Niu Zi, form into pills the size of mung beans. Take 30 to 50 pills without restriction, swallowed with light ginger soup; warm tea or warm wine are also good. For small children, the pills should be the size of corn grains, taken as before.

Clove Spleen Accumulation Pill
San Leng, peeled and stewed; E Zhu, stir-fried; and Shen Qu, stir-fried, each seven qian. Qing Pi, Ba Dou powder, Xiao Hui Xiang (fennel), stir-fried; Chen Pi, each five qian. Ding Xiang and Mu Xiang, each three qian.
This is ground into a fine powder and mixed with vinegar to adjust Shen Qu into a thick paste, then formed into pills the size of mung beans. Take five to seven pills, swallowed with ginger soup.

Three Huang Zhi Zhu Pill
Treats injuries, dampness, spicy and thick flavors that cause obstruction and discomfort. Zhi Shi and wheat, both stir-fried, Huang Qin, each five qian; Chuan Huang Lian, soaked in wine and stir-fried; Da Huang, wrapped in wet paper and stewed; Bai Zhu, each one tael.
These are made into powder, soaked in broth and steamed into pills the size of mung beans. Take 50 pills, swallowed with clear broth. Adjust the quantity according to the amount of injury, increase or decrease dosage as necessary.[64p]

Shenghui Herbal Powder
Used for treating children with undigested food, decreased appetite, thin limbs, and abdominal distension.
Ingredients: Three parts of hawthorn peel, ginseng, white atractylodes, slightly yellow roasted malt, dried orange peel, areca nut each half a coin; one part of honey-fried licorice.
Method: Grind the above ingredients into a coarse powder. Take one coin of the powder, mix with a small cup of water and decoct until reduced to a fifth. Strain, adjusting the dosage according to the child's size. Take warm, four to five times daily.

Zhu's Mu Xiang Pill
Used to stimulate appetite and aid digestion in children.
Ingredients: One ounce of sparganium, mu xiang, ginseng, white poria, green tangerine peel, dried tangerine peel, nutmeg each one coin.
Method: Grind into a fine powder, mix with water to form pills the size of sesame seeds. Take ten pills, swallowed with ginger soup.

Zhu's Washing Heart Powder
Used to treat children with heart damage from milk or food, who are feverish, wheezy, and excessively sleepy with a cough.
Ingredients: Half an ounce of soapberry, roasted with sand and sugar until charred, then let the fire cool. One coin of raw licorice, one and a half coins of ophiopogon.
Method: Grind together until finely powdered. Take two coins, mix with one cup of water and decoct until reduced to three-fifths, dividing into five doses to be taken at intervals.

Nourishing the Spleen Pill
Ingredients: One coin each of ginseng, white atractylodes, angelica sinensis, and chuanxiong; one coin each of mu xiang, green tangerine peel, coptis chinensis, and dried tangerine peel; five cents each of cardamom, hawthorn flesh, roasted shenqu, and roasted malt.
Method: Grind into a fine powder, mix with water to form pills about the size of sesame seeds. Take thirty to fifty pills with rice broth.[65p]

Li Hui Sanling San is used to treat solid masses in the breast. If there is stagnation of evil leading to accumulation that does not dissolve, it causes the child to become increasingly emaciated, with a pallid yellow complexion. This condition often occurs in spring and summer, and the child has little desire for milk or food.

The ingredients include: Sanling, flaked Dahuang (slightly fried), Bingtang, Guiqia (softened), and Chifeng, each at half a "liang"; Zhiqiao (roasted until slightly yellow) at two and a half "qian" each. These should be ground and sifted into a powder. The dosage: take one "qian" of the powder with a small cup of water, simmer until reduced to one-fifth, strain, and divide into two doses, taken three to four times a day to eliminate the pathogenic substances.

Zhang Huan's Sanling San is used to treat solid, unresolved masses in children's breasts. The ingredients include: Sanling, Chi Fu (rehmannia), Danggui (angelica), Guiqia (vinegar-baked and skirt removed), each at one "liang"; Zhiqiao (roasted), Muxiang (costus), and Baizhu (white atractylodes), each at half a "liang." These should be ground into a fine powder. The dosage: take one "qian" with a cup of water, add seven slices of fresh ginger, simmer until reduced to one-fifth, strain, allow to cool, and administer as needed.

Shenghui Huapi Wan is used to treat lumps of breast masses that have not dissolved for a long time, with no other medication proving effective. The ingredients include: half a "liang" of Ba Dou (castor bean); one "qian" each of Ni Fen (greasy powder) and Zhu Sha (cinnabar), ground; Nao Sha (sulfur), Xiong Que (male ginger), each one character portion; and two and a half "qian" of Huang Ying Jiang (yellow eagle ginger).

These ingredients should be ground into a fine powder. Mix with glutinous rice to form pills the size of millet. For a child of one year, take two pills on an empty stomach with a decoction of soap beans, to facilitate the elimination of pathogenic substances.[66p]

Mr. Mao's Thousand Gold Pill treats all kinds of accumulation diseases in children.

Ingredients:

  • Talcum powder
  • White sweet丁香
  • Tian Nan Xing
  • Light powder, each two qian
  • Mercury, two qian

First, melt two qian of tin in a copper pan, then add mercury, mix well, pour it onto the ground, and let it cool.

Next, use half a qian of Qingdai, and seventy-two peeled and pitted Ba Dou, ensuring none are damaged. Soak them in well water overnight, then hang them in the wind to dry, and grind them into a fine powder.

Combine the previous ingredients, and use soft rice to form pills the size of small mung beans. If Ba Dou does not exude oil, take them with soup.

For phlegm after a febrile disease, take onion soup. For intestinal parasites, take beef juice.

For convulsions, if the stomach feels tight and hard, and the face appears dark, use mint with onion soup.

In case of injury, if the stomach and abdominal skin feel slightly warm, with abdominal distension at night, presenting symptoms similar to intestinal worms but not quite the same, with a yellowish-green complexion and slightly yellow eyes, this indicates accumulation.

Use two to seven pieces of soapberry, baked over ash, and boil with one cup of water until reduced to half a cup.

For accumulated diarrhea, use fish vinegar soup. For gas accumulation, use fried fennel soup.

Generally, a child of one year should take fourteen pills, three years old eighteen pills, and seven years old twenty-four pills; adjust according to the child's size.

This medicine should be taken around four o'clock, so that it will clear by dawn. When treating an accumulation, adjust the medication based on the symptoms.

It is acceptable if a small amount of saliva is expelled before taking the medicine.[67p]

Five Color Pills: Used to treat all injuries in children, phlegm and drool blockage, chest and diaphragm discomfort, undigested milk and food, formation of masses, hardness in the sides, and pain upon pressure; also treats all types of sudden and chronic convulsions caused by phlegm and drool blockage.

　　六圣丸 【曾氏方，下同】 　治诸积和胃。大能主气，厚肠消疳快膈。　　莪朮炮　净黄连　陈皮　白姜炮，各五钱　南木香二钱半　　右除木香不见火，余四味銼焙，同木香为末，每一钱，巴豆三粒，去壳膜心存油碎切，入乳钵内细研，同前药再研匀，酢煮面糊丸麻仁大，每服十五粒至二十五粒，或三十五粒，五更空心淡姜汤下，利三五行，匀气散止补。此药常服肋脾化积，进食消疳，临睡以净汤或汤酒下三粒及五粒，每次止丸药末三钱，净巴豆九粒为则。不可多合，久则味散。[72p]

Six Holy Pills
[From the Zeng Family Prescription, as below]
Treats various accumulations and harmonizes the stomach. Greatly invigorates vital energy, strengthens the intestines, alleviates gnawing hunger, and quickly soothes the diaphragm.

Ingredients:

  • Prepared Atractylodes: 5 qian
  • Clean Huanglian: 5 qian
  • Aged Tangerine Peel: 5 qian
  • Prepared White Ginger: 5 qian
  • Southern Wood Fragrance: 2.5 qian

Excluding Southern Wood Fragrance from fire, crush and roast the other four ingredients together, then mix with Southern Wood Fragrance into a fine powder.

For each dose, take 1 qian of the mixture, 3 pieces of Ba Dou (castor seed), remove the shell and membrane, keeping the oily heart, chop finely, and grind in a mortar. Combine with the previous powder and grind again until uniform. Form into pills the size of a hemp seed, taking 15 to 25 pills each time, or up to 35. Consume on an empty stomach in the early morning with a weak ginger soup to promote bowel movement, regulate qi flow, and stop discomfort.

This medicine, when taken regularly, helps resolve rib and spleen accumulations, aids digestion after meals, and before sleep, take 3 to 5 pills with clean soup or wine. Each time, limit to 3 qian of powder and follow with 9 pieces of pure Ba Dou. Do not combine too much, as prolonged use may dilute the effectiveness.[72p]

　　乌犀丸　主诸积滞夹惊夹风，温胃调脾，消进饮食。吐逆酢馊气，面黄肌瘦，不拘孩儿生后岁月远近，并宜可投。　　乌犀即皂角，銼三寸长煨灰火中见青烟起为度，取出地上瓦碗盖定存性冷用，七钱　舶硫黄　白姜各三钱半　陈皮　川乌炮去皮脐，各五钱　巴豆去壳膜心存油，七十七粒　　右先研硫黄细，除巴豆外，余四味同焙为末，却薄切巴豆细研，同前五味药末捣匀，用粳米饭包作一大粽子，小瓦瓶盛水，熟煮候冷，取出沙钵内烂杵，细布兜紧，绞出如稠糊，安在别器内，以药末停分同杵细软，丸粟米大，取诸积每服十五丸、或五丸、或二十一丸，至三十三丸，并用淡姜汤泡冷饭取汁小盏，五更初空心送下。通利三五行，以匀气散止补。治积滞有酢馊气，每服三丸至五丸，用淡姜汤入米酢少许，候温空心下。[73p]

Wuxi Pill is used for various accumulations and stagnations, accompanied by chills and wind; it warms the stomach, regulates the spleen, and helps digest food and drink. It alleviates symptoms of nausea and rancid odors, and is suitable for anyone regardless of age after childbirth, whether recent or distant.

Wuxi refers to the soap pod. Cut it into three-inch pieces, roast in ashes until blue smoke appears, then remove and place it in a cool earthenware bowl to preserve its coolness. Measure seven qian of ship sulfur, three and a half qian each of white ginger, dried tangerine peel, and Sichuan black cardamom (skin and navel removed), and five qian each of the remaining ingredients.

For preparation, first grind the sulfur finely, and except for the horse bean, roast the other four ingredients into a powder. Then thinly slice the horse bean and grind it finely; combine this with the four powdered ingredients. Wrap the mixture in glutinous rice to form a large rice dumpling, and place it in a small earthenware pot filled with water to cook until soft. Once cooled, use a mortar and pestle to mash it up, then strain it through fine cloth to extract a thick paste, and store it in a separate container. Mix the powdered medicine evenly with the prepared paste and form into pills the size of millet grains.

For any accumulation, take fifteen pills, or alternatively five, or twenty-one to thirty-three pills, accompanied by a small cup of cold ginger soup with rice juice, taken early in the morning on an empty stomach. It promotes overall circulation and dissipates stagnation. For treating accumulations with rancid odors, take three to five pills, using light ginger soup with a little rice vinegar, warmed and taken on an empty stomach.[73p]

　　水晶丹　治惊积食积虫积，腹胀烦啼，恶心，食减面黄，并宜通利。此药有顽积惊重，风紧涎多，热极，乃可服，非常用之剂。及急惊后，风痰未尽，免生痴疾，宜再投。　　南星銼不块汤煮片时　半夏汤泡去滑，各三钱　滑石四钱　轻粉五十贴　净芜荑二百片　巴豆五十粒，去壳汤泡七次，又去心膜作两半，水煮少时，晒干碎切　　右前三味焙为末，拌和轻粉外，芜荑、巴豆同碎切在乳钵内，细杵入前药末，再拌匀，如乌犀丸内制糊，丸麻仁大，每服十五丸至二十五丸，或三十五丸，糯米汤泡葱白，取汁小盏，五更初空心下，过三五行，进匀气散调补。下风痰，淡姜汤空心服。[74p]

Crystal Elixir treats symptoms such as fright, food accumulation, parasitic infestations, abdominal bloating, restlessness, nausea, reduced appetite, and pallor. It is also effective for promoting bowel movements. This medication is used for severe cases of fright and accumulation, with symptoms of tight winds and excessive saliva, or extreme heat. It should not be taken casually. After a sudden fright and if wind phlegm persists, it is advisable to take it again to prevent the development of dementia.

Preparation involves using Nanjing star herb (Zhuzhu) without blocks, boiling sections of pinellia tuber, soaking in water to remove slickness, using each herb in a quantity of three qian (about 9 grams), with friable talc at four qian, light powder at fifty shreds, two hundred pieces of clean artemisia, and fifty seeds of fruit from the croton tree, which should have the shells removed and soaked in water seven times, then cut in half, boiled briefly, and dried before being chopped finely.

The first three herbs are roasted into a powder and mixed with the light powder. The artemisia and croton seeds are chopped finely in a mortar, then mixed with the previously powdered herbs until uniformly combined, forming a dough similar to wuhui pills, each the size of a sesame seed. Each dose consists of fifteen to twenty-five pills, or up to thirty-five, to be taken with a small dish of scallion juice made from glutinous rice, consumed on an empty stomach at dawn, spaced three to five movements apart to promote circulation and balance. For expelling wind phlegm, take a light ginger decoction on an empty stomach.[74p]

　　聚宝圣饼子　取一切积，及虚中积，下风涎药，取病甚稳，全不搜搅。　　轻粉　粉霜各四钱　石燕子大者二枚，为细末　延胡索大者二十八个，为末　　右四味，同研匀，滴水和丸如大棋子大，仍放候阴干，每服一饼，先用熟水浸软，冷浆水调下，临卧更深。服后急漱口。此药只取积滞，并不损气，更临时加减。若下惊积，则每料更入朱砂、生龙脑各一钱，小儿一饼作四服，或便捏成小饼子。[75p]

Zhang's Method for Treating Children's Milk Bumps:
One tael of wildflower, soaked in vinegar and washed clean after three days, and half a tael of rhubarb. Dong's Method for Treating Children's Milk Bumps, Extremely Effective:
Two taels of purple river vehicle and three taels of cold food flour. Grind these into a fine powder. Each time, use about a spoonful mixed with water to apply to the soles of the feet. If the problem is on the left, apply to the left; if on the right, apply to the right. Wrap it in red silk and leave it for a long time. The ailment will pass out with the stool, saving many people. After the stool is eliminated, wash it away.

Kong's Method for Treating Children's Milk Bumps:
Mituo monk, no specific amount required, ground into a very fine powder. Mix this with the natural juice of garlic to the right consistency and apply to the area with milk bumps, ensuring thorough coverage without excessive application. Wait a moment until the child has a garlic breath, which indicates the medicine has penetrated. Carefully massage with your hand until the milk bumps seem to reduce by about fifty to sixty percent, then wash it away with warm diluted milk. It is crucial to gauge the amount; do not let it disappear completely, fearing the medicinal poison may harm the energy. If it hasn't dissolved and the medicine dries out, moisten it with warm water.[78p]

　　外台必效方　疗小儿癖。
　　车下李仁微汤退去皮及双仁，与干面相半捣之　　右为饼，如犹干，和淡水，如常搜面，大小一如病人手掌，为两饼，微炙使黄，勿令至熟，空肚食一枚，当快利。如不利，更食一枚。或饮热粥汁即利。以快利为度。至午后利不止，即以酢饭止之。利后当虚。病未尽者，量力一二日更尽一服，以病尽为限。小儿亦以意量之。不得食酪及牛马肉，无不效。但病重者，李仁与面相半，轻者以意减之，亦须量力。频试无不瘥，神效。
　　圣惠前胡丸　治小儿癖气腹痛。
　　前胡　桔梗各去芦　赤芍　赤茯　枳壳　川大黄　当归　郁李仁去皮微炒，各半两　鳖甲一两，炙令黄　　右件捣罗为末，炼蜜为丸如菉豆大，三岁儿每服空心，以粥饮化破五丸服，量儿大小加减。一方无桔梗，亦作散服。[83p]

Outer Platform Must Follow the Prescription for Treating Childhood Disorders.

For a child’s disorder, take the peeled Li Ren (apricot kernel) and double kernels, remove the skin, and pound them together with dry flour. Form into cakes; if too dry, mix with plain water, shaping them to the size of the patient’s palm to make two cakes. Lightly roast them until they are yellow, but do not let them cook completely. Eat one on an empty stomach; it should be effective. If not effective, eat another one. Drinking hot congee can also aid efficiency. Efficiency is the measure. If by afternoon the condition doesn't improve, stop with vinegar rice. After passing, the patient should feel weak. If the illness has not fully resolved, based on what can be tolerated, take an additional dose after one or two days, limiting it to the end of the illness. For children, also gauge as needed. They must avoid eating dairy and beef or horse meat, as there will be no benefit. For those with severe illness, reduce the amount of Li Ren with flour; for lighter cases, adjust accordingly while still measuring strength. With repeated trials, efficacy is guaranteed, achieving remarkable results.

Holy Benefit Qian Hu Pill for Treating Childhood Disorders and Abdominal Pain.

Take equal parts of Qian Hu (Peucedanum) and Jie Geng (Platycodon) without the reeds, as well as Chi Shao (Red Peony), Chi Fu (Red Rehmannia), Zhi Ke (Bitter Orange), Chuan Da Huang (Rhubarb), Angelica (Dang Gui), and Yu Li Ren (Black Plum Kernel) with skins removed and lightly roasted, each half a tael. Add one tael of tortoise shell, roasted until yellow. Grind these ingredients and sift into a fine powder, then combine with honey to form pills the size of mung beans. For a three-year-old, dissolve five pills in congee to ingest on an empty stomach, adjusting the amount based on the child's size. If lacking Jie Geng, it can also be taken as a powder.[83p]

Fu Ling Decoction: Treats children's tics with a robust fever. Frequent use of cold medicines has created a cold condition in the heart, and the lower body is also cold, resulting in constipation with difficult bowel movements.

Chai Hu Decoction: Treats children aged 7 or 8 who sleep excessively, or sometimes exhibit robust fever, progressively becoming frail, though not in pain, occasionally having dysentery with pus, vomiting, and loss of appetite. To regulate the chest barrier and alleviate discomfort from reduced food intake. It also helps to soothe qi, harmonize the stomach, and eliminate retained food.

Eight Counteracting Ointment
[From "Shenjing Tongkao Fang"]
For treating small children's masses and fevers.
Five qian of borax, two liang each of gardenia fruit, natron, and ligusticum oil, one chicken egg, one liang of white radish peel, five scallion whites (with roots), one wine cup of honey, paper to stick and wrap in silk.

Single Prescription
For children's milk lumps, elevated chest and abdomen, wheezing, and vomiting milk: Use seven peeled black beans, grind them very fine, and drip water on them seven times to make seven pills. Roll in indigo powder until fully coated, then wrap the medicine in wheat flour dough and steam until cooked. Remove the dough, grind finely again, add a little greasy powder, fresh brain, and musk, then drip water to make seven pills again. Take one pill with warm water before sleeping. If the child chews it, it is fine, very effective.

For children's illnesses: Use two liang of musk meat, chop and roast it, three hundred Sichuan peppers, stir-fry, and crush into powder. Mix with egg white to make pills the size of small beans. Take two or three pills with soup to gauge proper dosage. [From "Fan Wang Fang"][87p]

　　治小儿食不知饥饱：用鼠屎二七枚烧为末，服之。 【《千金方》，下同】
　　治小儿食土：取肉一斤，绳系曳地行数里，勿洗，火炙与食。
　　小儿闪癖：取苦瓠未破者，煮苓熟，解开熨之。 【《陈藏器本草》】　　又：以巴豆一粒，同枳壳一枚，切作二片，去穰内巴豆，以麻系合，不拘多少，水煮，令枳壳软烂，则去巴豆，焙干枳壳为末，面糊丸如桐子大，食后熟水下十五丸。老人小儿皆可服之。【《退斋雅闻录》】
　　小儿吃土：用干黄土一块研末，浓煎黄连汤调下。 【《救急方》】
　　小儿痞积：急性子、水红花、大黄各一两，俱生研末，每味取五钱，外用皮硝一两拌匀；将白鹁鸽一个，或白鸭亦可，去毛屎，剖腹，勿犯水，以布拭净，将末装入内，用绵扎定，沙锅内用水三碗，重重纸封，以小火煮干，将鸽鸭翻调焙黄色，冷定，早晨食之，日四时，疾软，三日大便下血，病去矣。忌冷物百日。【《孙天仁集效方》】[88p]

For treating a child's inability to recognize hunger and satiety: Use two to seven mouse droppings, burn them to a powder, and administer.

For treating a child who eats dirt: Take one pound of meat, tie it to a rope and drag it on the ground for several miles without washing it, then roast it and let the child eat.

For a child's excessive gathering habit: Take an unbroken bitter gourd, cook it with sweet flag until soft, then unwrap and iron it. Additionally: Use one seed of cowbane with one piece of bitter orange peel, cut into two slices, remove the inner seeds of the cowbane, and bind the pieces with hemp. Boil them in water until the bitter orange peel is soft, then remove the cowbane, dry the peel, and grind it into powder. Make balls the size of pine nuts and take fifteen of them with warm water after meals. Both the elderly and children can take this.

For a child eating dirt: Use a piece of dry yellow earth, grind it to powder, and mix it with strong decoction of Huang Lian (Coptis) to take.

For a child's abdominal distension: Take one tael each of raw impatience, safflower, and rhubarb, grind them together. Take five qian of each of these ingredients. Mix one tael of calcium carbonate (liuli) externally. Use one white pigeon or a white duck, remove its feathers, clean the excrement, and split open its belly without getting it wet. Wipe it clean with a cloth and fill its belly with the powder, securing it with cotton. In a clay pot, add three bowls of water, seal it tightly with paper, then simmer until dry. Roast the pigeon or duck until it turns yellow, let it cool, and consume it in the morning. Do this four times a day, and if symptoms worsen for three days with blood in the stool, the illness will be resolved. Avoid cold substances for a hundred days.[88p]

　　小儿痞块腹大，肌瘦面黄，渐成疳疾：使君子仁三钱，木鳖子仁五钱为末，水丸龙眼大，每以一丸用鸡子一个，破顶入药在内，饭上蒸熟，空心食之。【《杨氏简便方》】
　　小儿脾癖疳积：锦纹大黄三两为末，酢一盏，沙锅内文武火熬成膏，倾瓦上，日晒夜露，三日再研，用舶上硫黄一两，形如琥珀者，官粉一两同研匀。十岁以下小儿半钱，米饮下。忌一切生冷鱼肉，只食白粥。半月前一服不愈，半月之后再服。若不忌口，不如勿服。【《圣济总录》】

　　小儿诸果成积，伤脾作胀，气急：用麝香一钱，生桂末一两，饭和丸菉豆大，大人十五丸，小儿七丸，白汤下。盖果得麝则落，木得桂则枯故也。【《济生方》】[89p]

A child with an enlarged abdomen, thin muscles, and a yellow face gradually develops a malnourished condition. Take three qian of the seeds of the Sophora japonica and five qian of the seeds of the Trichosanthes kirilowii, grind them into a powder, and form pills the size of longan. Each pill should be taken with one egg, the top of which is broken to insert the medicine inside, then steam on rice until cooked, and eat on an empty stomach.

For children with abdominal distension due to accumulation: take three liang of large yellow rhubarb, grind it to a powder, mix it with one cup of vinegar, and simmer it in a clay pot over low and high heat until it becomes a paste. Pour it onto a tile and let it dry in the sun by day and dew by night for three days, then grind it again, adding one liang of sulfur resembling amber, and one liang of official powder, mixing well. For children under ten years old, take half a qian with rice wine. Avoid all raw and cold fish and meat, only eat plain congee. If it does not improve after half a month, take it again after another half a month. If the diet is not restricted, it is better not to take the medicine.

For children's growth issues: take four liang of angelica root, grind it into a powder, and take one sheep's liver, split it open with a bamboo knife, sprinkle the powder inside, tie it up with thread, then boil it in a clay pot until cooked, and crush it into pills for oral administration.

For children with a buildup of fruits causing spleen damage and bloating, leading to shortness of breath: use one qian of musk and one liang of ground cinnamon, mix with rice to form pills the size of mung beans. Adults should take fifteen pills, while children should take seven and wash down with clear soup. This is because when fruits are combined with musk, they drop, and wood combined with cinnamon becomes brittle.[89p]

　　小儿症瘕：用老鼠肉煮汁作粥食之。 【《姚和众方》】

For children's conditions related to phlegm: use mouse meat to boil juice and make congee.

For children with sparse, yellow hair and who are thin and weak: grind dried apple slices into powder, mix with vinegar, and apply.

For children's qi disorders: boil three-edged needle to make broth or congee, and let the wet nurse eat dates to give to the child. For newborns up to a hundred days and those under ten years old, regardless of sick conditions such as epilepsy or disorders, the treatment is profound and effective.

For treating children who eat dirt or have stomach issues: use one part greasy powder, mix with sugar to form pills the size of hemp seeds, and let the child drink with hollow rice; upon expelling the dirt, they will recover.

For children eating soil: take good soil, cook strong Huanlian to extract clear juice, dry it, and administer; once taken, the issue will cease.

　　治脾胃不和，呕逆恶心，乳食不进：厚朴姜制一钱，白朮半钱，干姜炮、甘草炙各三分，水一盏，姜二片煎，空心热服。
　　治宿食伤脾，消食快膈：缩砂仁、三棱、莪朮、神曲、麦芽各半两，香附子一两各炒为末，面和丸如麻子大，食后白汤下，随大小加减丸数。
　　小儿癖积：用粪中蛆洗净晒干为末，入甘草末少许，米糊丸梧子大，每服五七丸，米饮下甚妙。【《总微论》】
　　小儿疳积有痰：用南星一两，半夏五钱，水泡七次，切片，用姜一两捣汁浸，以不麻为度；甘草、白附子各五钱，水滴为丸，紫苏汤下五分。【《幼幼近编》，下同】
　　一小儿吃粽成腹痛：用黄连、白酒药为末服之愈。
　　　　针灸
　　]

　　晋皇甫谧《甲乙经》曰：小儿食晦头痛，譩嘻主之。　　小儿口中腥臭，胸胁搘满，劳宫主之。　　小儿嗽而泄不欲食者，商丘主之。[91p]

To treat disharmony of the spleen and stomach, with symptoms of vomiting and nausea, and inability to consume milk or food: Take 1 qian of thick-foliated magnolia bark, 0.5 qian of white atractylodes, 3 fen each of prepared dried ginger and honey-fried licorice, boil them in 1 cup of water with 2 slices of ginger, and take it hot on an empty stomach.

To treat food stagnation injuring the spleen and facilitate digestion: Take 0.5 liang each of cardamom, notopterygium, rhizoma dioscoreae, fermented wheat, and malt, and 1 liang of cyperus fried to a powder. Mix with flour to form pills the size of sesame seeds, and consume them with rice soup after meals, adjusting the number of pills according to size.

For children's accumulation of phlegm: Clean and dry maggots from dung, powder them, adding a little licorice powder, and form into pills the size of walnuts. Take 5 to 7 pills with rice wine—it is very effective.

For children's malnutrition with phlegm: Take 1 liang of south star herb and 5 qian of pinellia, soak in water seven times, slice, and use 1 liang of ginger to extract juice for soaking until not numbing; add 5 qian each of licorice and white atractylodes, form into pills with water, and take 5 fen with perilla soup.

A child who experiences abdominal pain after eating dumplings: Take powdered coptis and white liquor and consume to alleviate the condition.

Acupuncture
Jin's Huanfu Mi in the "Jia Yi Jing" states: For children's headache from food stagnation, it is governed by Mu Min. For children with a foul smell in the mouth and fullness in the chest and sides, it is governed by Lao Gong. For children who cough and have diarrhea with no desire to eat, it is governed by Shang Qiu.[91p]

　　小儿腹满不能食饮，悬钟主之。
　　《千金方》曰：治小儿癖，灸两乳下一寸各三壮。　　《古今医统》曰：小儿癖气，灸章门、脊中；积聚泻泄痃癖，于十一椎下两旁，相去各一寸五分，灸七壮。　　王肯堂《证治准绳》曰：小儿癖气久不瘥者，灸中脘一穴、章门二穴各七壮。章门在大横外直脐，季胁肋端，侧卧，曲上足伸下足，举臂取之。中脘在上脘下一寸，脐上四寸，居心蔽骨与脐之中，从(暍去日改骨)骭下取病人四指定穴。并灸脐后脊骨中二七壮，无不验。　　《古今医鉴》曰：灸癖法，穴在小儿背脊中，自尾骶骨将手揣摸脊骨，两傍有血筋发动处两穴，每一穴用铜钱三文，压在穴上，用艾烟[艾烟　疑当作「艾炷」。]安钱孔中，各灸七壮。此是癖之根，贯血之所，灸之疮即发，即可见效。灸不着血筋，则疮不发而不效矣。[92p]

If a child experiences abdominal fullness and is unable to eat or drink, the treatment involves using moxibustion on the Xuan Zhong point.

The "Qian Jin Fang" states: To treat children with intestinal issues, perform moxibustion three times an inch below each nipple. The "Gu Jin Yi Tong" mentions that for children with phlegm issues, apply moxibustion on the Zhang Men and along the spine; for accumulation and diarrhea issues, perform moxibustion seven times on both sides near the lower part of the eleventh vertebra, about one and a half inches apart.

Wang Kentang's "Zheng Zhi Zhun Sheng" states that if a child's phlegm condition does not resolve after a long time, moxibustion seven times each on the Zhong Wan point and the two Zhang Men points is indicated. The Zhang Men point is located on the lateral side, directly outside the navel, at the edge of the ribcage below the left and right armpits. The child should lie sideways, bend one leg up and extend the other down, raising the arm to access the points. The Zhong Wan point is one inch below the upper abdominal point, four inches above the navel, located between the heart's covering bones and the navel itself. After finding the appropriate points, apply moxibustion seven times in total on the area around the navel and the mid-spine, without exception.

The "Gu Jin Yi Jian" explains that for phlegm treatment, the moxibustion points are in the center of the child's back, starting from the tailbone and feeling along the spine for two points where the blood vessels are active. For each point, place a three-wen copper coin on it and burn mugwort in the coin's hole, moxibustion seven times. These are the root points for phlegm, where blood flows. If moxibustion is applied properly, lesions will appear and effects can be seen; if it does not reach the blood vessels, then lesions will not appear and the treatment will be ineffective.[92p]

　　　　医案

　　钱乙《小儿直诀》曰：曹宣德子三岁，面黄，时发寒热，不欲食而饮水，及乳不止，众医以为潮热，用牛黄丸、麝香丸不愈，及以止渴干葛散服之反吐。钱曰：当下白饼子，后补脾。乃以消积丸磨之，此乃癖也。后果愈。何以故？不食但饮水者，食伏于管内不能消，致令发寒热。服止渴药吐者，以药冲脾故也，下之即愈。
　　罗天益《卫生宝鉴》曰：真定总管董公长孙，年十一岁，病癖积，左胁下硬如覆手，肚大青筋，发热肌热，咳嗽自汗，日晡尤甚，牙疳臭恶，宣露出血，四肢困倦，饮食减少，病甚危笃，召太医刘仲安先生治之，约百日可愈。先与沉香海金沙丸一服，下秽物两三行；次日合塌气丸服之；十日复以沉香海金沙丸导利之，又令服塌气丸。如此互换，服至月余，其癖减半，未及百日良愈。近年多有此疾，愈之者多，录之以救将来之病者。[93p]

Medical Case

Qian Yi in "Pediatric Direct Method" states: Cao Xuande's son, three years old, had a yellow complexion, intermittent fevers, lacked appetite while excessively drinking water, and could not stop vomiting after drinking milk. Various doctors believed it to be tidal fever and treated it with cattle bile pills and musk pills without improvement. When using a thirst-quenching decoction, he vomited. Qian concluded: "A white cake should be given to clear the body, and then tonify the spleen." So, he ground up digestion pills, determining it was a form of accumulation. Eventually, the child recovered. Why? The lack of food and excessive drinking caused food to stagnate in the intestines, leading to intermittent fevers. Vomiting after taking thirst-quenching medicine happened due to the medicine clashing with the spleen; once purged, recovery followed.

Luo Tianyi in "Precious Mirror of Health" mentions: The overall governor of Zhen Ding, Dong Gong's eldest grandson, aged eleven, suffered from accumulation and hard masses under the left rib, a distended abdomen with visible veins, fevers, warm skin, coughing with spontaneous sweating, particularly severe in the afternoon, foul breath from dental issues, bleeding gums, and fatigue in the limbs, with reduced appetite; the illness was quite critical. The imperial physician Liu Zhong'an was summoned for treatment and estimated recovery in about a hundred days. He was first given a dose of agarwood and sea sand pills, which expelled two or three bowel movements; the next day, he took a flatulence pill; after ten days, he repeated the agarwood and sea sand pills for relief, followed by another dose of the flatulence pills. This interchange continued for over a month, with the accumulation halving, and within a hundred days, he was fully recovered. In recent years, this ailment has become more common, and many have recovered; it is recorded to aid future patients.[93p]

　　《汤氏小儿方》曰：户部张侍郎小娘子，患此蕴积结聚，已经年矣。其候腹满壮热，大小便闭，不食。诸医皆作虚热潮热。或作胃寒不食治。然既不食，大小便自然少。又欲作疳热治，百药俱试而无一中，势已窘迫，招予视之。问曰：合服何药？答曰：当服甘遂、大黄。涨惊骇曰：前诸医者，皆用补剂。此女不进饮食久矣，不宜利动肠胃。予答曰：信我者生，逆我者死。张曰：更有无甘遂而次于此药方者可否？予令即服大承气汤。二服而愈。次日诊之，尚有余滞积实，其证必过数日而复闭，须服前药，始可除根。数日后，果再闭，腹满痞结，再投此药，一服而痊。
　　《保婴金镜录》曰：一小儿人中青黄，嗳腐酸气，用平胃散一服，宿滞顿化，余云不必多药，但节其饮食自愈。不信，复伤食而嗳腐，另用克滞之药，更加吐泻以致不救。惜夫！[94p]

"The Young Child's Formulas" states: The young lady of Deputy Minister Zhang from the Ministry of Revenue has suffered from a long-standing accumulation of stagnation and blockages. She experiences a distended abdomen with strong heat, constipation, and a loss of appetite. All the doctors diagnosed her with a condition of deficient heat and fever. Some attributed her symptoms to a cold stomach, suggesting treatments for loss of appetite. However, her lack of eating naturally resulted in less urination and defecation. They considered treating her with remedies for malnutrition, but after trying various medicines without success, her condition had become dire, prompting them to request my assistance. Upon being asked which medicines should be taken, I advised them to use Gan Sui and Da Huang. They were alarmed, saying that previous doctors had only prescribed tonics. This young woman had not eaten or drunk for a long time; thus, it was not appropriate to stimulate her intestines and stomach. I replied, "Those who trust me will live; those who oppose me will die." Zhang then inquired if there were alternative recipes without Gan Sui. I instructed them to administer the Da Cheng Qi Decoction immediately. After two doses, she recovered. The next day, upon examination, there was still some residual blockages, and it was certain that within a few days, the condition would reoccur. She needed to take the previous medicine again to eliminate the root cause. A few days later, when she indeed faced blockage again, with a distended abdomen and hardness, after taking the medicine once more, she was completely cured.

"The Golden Mirror of Infant Care" states: A child exhibited a pale yellow complexion and burped sour gas. After administering a dose of Ping Wei San, the accumulated food was rapidly digested. I mentioned that there was no need for many medicines, just regulate their diet for recovery. However, not believing this, they caused further food injuries, resulting in burping and sourness. They used other medicines to combat the stagnation, leading to increased vomiting and diarrhea, ultimately resulting in a critical situation. Such a pity![94p]

　　一小儿伤食呕吐，服克伐之药，呕中见血，用清热凉血之药，又大便下血，唇色白而或青，问其故于余。余曰：此脾土亏损，肝木所乘而然也。令空心服补中益气汤。食远用异功散，以调补中气，使涎血各归其源而愈。
　　《体仁汇编》曰：昔有一人从贵州来得瘴，夫妇相继而死，存二子归，皆病，腹中有块如瓜，其苦欲死。用大黄酒洗、荜拨微炙，等分为细末，蜜丸桐子大，每服五十丸，空心麝香水送下。方十服，气块皆消。此方小儿做小丸用，大人大丸。初服五十丸，以后只逐日二十丸或服三十丸，不可太多，病去八分止服，以俟自消尽也。
　　《薛氏医案》曰：一小儿伤食，发热唇动，或用养胃汤、枳实、黄连、山楂之类，更加腹胀，午后发热，按其腹不痛。余以为服前药，饮食虽化而脾胃复伤也，用六君子汤数剂而痊。[95p]

A young child ate too much and vomited. After taking a remedy, there was blood in the vomit, and then he had bloody stools. His lips were pale and sometimes blue. When asked for the reason, I said: "This is due to the deficiency of the spleen, which is overpowered by the liver." I instructed him to take the "Buzhong Yiqi Decoction" on an empty stomach. After a while, use "Yigong Powder" to regulate and nourish the middle energy, allowing the fluids and blood to return to their source and heal.

The "Tirén Huibian" states: "Once there was a person who came from Guizhou and contracted malaria. The couple died one after the other, leaving behind two sons who were both ill, with lumps in their abdomen like melons, suffering painfully. I used rhubarb wine to wash it, combined with slightly roasted pepper, ground them into a fine powder and mixed them equally, forming honey pills the size of tung seeds. Each dose consisted of fifty pills, taken with musk water on an empty stomach. After ten doses, all the gas lumps disappeared. For children, smaller pills were used, while adults used larger ones. Initially, fifty pills were consumed, and afterward only twenty or thirty pills daily were taken. Avoid excessive doses; once 80% of the illness was alleviated, stop taking to allow complete recovery."

The "Xue's Medical Records" notes: "A young child had overeaten, developed a fever, and unusual lip movements. Remedies like 'Stomach Nourishing Decoction', bitter orange, coptis, and hawthorn were used, but the child experienced further abdominal bloating and afternoon fevers. Upon examination, the abdomen wasn’t painful. I believed that while previous medicines might have digested food, they harmed the spleen and stomach. I administered several doses of 'Liu Jun Zi Decoction' and he recovered."[95p]

　　一小儿伤食，风热呕吐，唇口蠕动，服消导清热之剂，饮食已消，热犹如故。余曰：此胃经虚热耳。用四君子、升麻、柴胡四剂而愈。
　　一小儿素面白，忽然目唇微动，时面色黄青，良久，其唇口手足亦微动，此脾虚而肝侮之也，用五味异功散加钓藤钩、白附子一剂而面青少退，再二剂唇口动亦止，又用异功散加升麻柴胡四剂而痊。
　　治一小儿腹中痞塞，却服二陈、枳实、黄连，其痞益甚。余谓：属脾经血虚。用六君子加当归，数剂胃气渐复；乃朝用异功散加升麻，夕用异功散加当归而愈。
　　一小儿未及周岁，气短喘急，乳食少进，时或吐乳，视其形如去蛇，乃脾伤而食积，先用六君子加山楂、枳实，渐愈；后乳食复伤，吐泻作渴，候二日不止，先与胃苓膏以治吐泻，继以七味白朮散生胃气而愈。[96p]

A small child had a food injury, experiencing wind-heat vomiting, with lips and mouth twitching. After taking a digestive and heat-clearing medicine, the food had digested, but the heat remained unchanged. I said: this is due to deficient stomach qi and excess heat. I used Four Gentlemen Decoction, Shengma, and Chaihu, and the child recovered.

Another small child had a pale face and suddenly showed slight movements of the lips. At times, the complexion turned yellow and green. After a long while, the lips, mouth, hands, and feet also showed slight movements. This was due to spleen deficiency being insulted by the liver. I used Wuwu Yigong Powder with added Diaoteng and Bai Fuzhi, and the complexion improved slightly. After two more doses, the movements of the lips and mouth ceased. I then used Yigong Powder with Shengma and Chaihu and achieved recovery.

For a small child with abdominal distension, I initially gave Erchen Tang, Zhi Shi, and Huang Lian, but the distension worsened. I diagnosed a deficiency of blood in the spleen. I used Six Gentlemen Decoction with added Dang Gui, and after several doses, the stomach qi gradually recovered. Then, in the morning, I used Yigong Powder with Shengma, and in the evening, I used Yigong Powder with Dang Gui, leading to recovery.

A small child under one year old experienced shortness of breath and wheezing, had a poor appetite for milk, and occasionally vomited it. The child appeared emaciated, indicating spleen damage and food accumulation. I first used Six Gentlemen Decoction with Shan Zha and Zhi Shi, and the child gradually improved. Later, milk and food injuries caused vomiting and diarrhea with thirst. After waiting two days without relief, I first gave Wei Ling Gao to treat the vomiting and diarrhea, followed by Qi Wei Bai Zhu San to generate stomach qi, resulting in recovery.[96p]

　　一小儿患痞，服克滞之药。余谓：形气有余，病气有余者，当泻不当补；形气不足，病气不足者，当补不当泻。前证属形病俱虚，非调补中气不愈。不信，仍行克伐，元气亏损，虚火上炎，齿龈蚀烂，颔下结核，余用大芜荑汤及异功散之类，寻愈。
　　一小儿停食发热，服芩、连、三棱等剂，饮食日少，胸腹膨胀，肢体羸瘦。余谓脾虚饮食停滞，元气复伤，先用补中益气汤加木香、钓藤钩数剂渐愈，又用六君、炮姜调理而安。
　　一小儿素嗜肉食，腹中作痛，大便不调，半载之后，肚腹膨胀，右胁内结一块，不时转移；又三月，左胁内亦结一块，胸腹亦胀，龈溃作渴，小便赤濇或澄白，大便色秽不一；又半载，颔下结核三五枚。服消块行滞等药，元气益虚，其块益甚。余用四味肥儿丸、五味异功散之类，随证进退治之，热渴渐止；又月余，腹胀渐消，更佐以九味芦荟丸，齿龈渐愈；乃用四君子汤为主，佐以芜荑丸之类而痊。[97p]

A young child suffered from a distended belly and took medicine to eliminate stagnation. I believed that when both the physical and pathological qi are excessive, purging should be done, not tonifying; when both are deficient, tonifying should be done, not purging. The previous symptoms indicated a deficiency in both the physical and pathological aspects, and merely tonifying the middle qi would not lead to recovery. Disbelieving this, they continued to attack the condition, resulting in a depletion of original qi, leading to virtual heat rising, causing gum erosion and submandibular nodules. I used a large dose of herbs like Dahuang and others, and the child soon recovered.

Another child had a loss of appetite accompanied by fever, took herbs such as Qiong and Lian, but their food intake decreased daily, leading to abdominal distension and emaciation. I noted that the spleen was weak and food was stagnating, resulting in further damage to the original qi. I first used the Bu Zhong Yi Qi Decoction, adding a few doses of Muscone and other ingredients, which gradually improved the condition. I then used Liujun Decoction and fried ginger for regulation and stabilization.

A child who loved to eat meat experienced abdominal pain with irregular bowel movements. After half a year, their abdomen swelled, and a hard lump formed in the right side, occasionally shifting. Three months later, another lump formed in the left side, and there was abdominal distension, with sore gums and thirst. Their urine was either reddish and thin or clear, and their stool color was inconsistent and foul. After another half year, three to five nodules appeared under the jaw. They took medicines to dissolve lumps and eliminate stagnation, depleting their original qi further and worsened the lumps. I used the Si Wei Fei Er Wan and Wu Wei Yi Gong San, adjusting treatment according to the symptoms, which gradually alleviated the thirst and heat. After about a month, the abdominal distension began to decrease, and I added Jiu Wei Lu Hui Wan, leading to gradual healing of the gums. Finally, I used Si Jun Zi Tang as the main prescription, supplemented with Wutou Wan among other herbs, resulting in complete recovery.[97p]

　　一小儿饮食不节，或作泻，或腹痛，或腹胀，腹中一块，大便不调，作渴发热，龈烂口臭，专服消导克滞，前证益甚，形体益瘦。余曰：面色黄中隐青，脾土亏损而肝木所侮也。法当调补中气平肝木，则脾气自旺，虚火自退，诸证自愈。遂月冲和汤、大芜荑汤之类，果愈。
　　一小儿小腹胀坠，小便濇滞，午前为甚，以补中益气汤加木香与朝服，以五味异功散加升麻、柴胡与夕服，两月余而愈。后饮食失节，腹胀咽酸，用五味异功散、四味茱萸丸而痊。毕姻后，复患如前，更恶寒腹冷，小便清频，大便不实，手足并冷，用补中益气汤、八味地黄丸而寻愈。[98p]

A young child has irregular eating habits, sometimes experiencing diarrhea, abdominal pain, or bloating, with a hard lump in the abdomen and irregular bowel movements. The child feels thirsty with a fever, and has swollen gums and bad breath. The treatment of using digestive aids only exacerbates the prior symptoms, leading to further weight loss. I remarked: the complexion is yellow with a hint of green, indicating depletion of the spleen and insult from the liver. The method should be to harmonize and replenish the central qi while calming the liver to strengthen the spleen’s qi, thus naturally relieving the fire of deficiency and allowing all symptoms to heal. Consequently, herbal formulas such as the Monthly Harmonizing Decoction and Large Artemisia Decoction were administered, and the child was indeed cured.

Another young child presented with lower abdominal distension and difficulty urinating, especially worse in the morning. A decoction to replenish the central qi and boost energy was prescribed, adding costus as well as a morning formula, while a modified version of Five-Flavored Decoction with added Cimicifuga and Bupleurum was given at night. After over two months, the child recovered. However, after a loss of dietary regulation, the child experienced abdominal bloating and sour belching, for which Five-Flavored Decoction and Four-Ingredient Euonymus Pill were used, leading to a cure. Later, after a marriage, the child fell ill again with similar symptoms, compounded by severe cold, abdominal chill, clear frequent urination, and unsettled stools, with cold hands and feet. The treatment involved the Replenishing Central Qi Decoction and Eight-Ingredient Rehmannia Pill, which soon brought recovery.[98p]

　　一小儿伤食腹胀，胸满有痰，余用异功散而痊。后复伤食，腹胀作痛，或用药下之，痛虽止而胀益甚，更加喘粗，此脾气伤而及于肺也，用六君、桔梗调补而愈。
　　一小儿腹胀，恶食，寒热恶心，证类外感。余曰：气口脉大于人迎，此饮食停滞也，用保和丸一服，诸证顿退，但腹胀未已，用异功散而痊。
　　一小儿伤风咳嗽痰涌，用六君、桔梗、桑皮、杏仁而愈。后饮食停滞，腹泻胀痛，又用六君加山楂、厚朴而安。复停食作呕，或用药下之，更加咳嗽。余谓：此脾肺益虚，欲行调补。彼以为缓，乃服发表克滞之药，前证益甚，更加摇头。余用天麻散倍加钓藤钩及异功散而愈。[99p]

A young child experienced abdominal distension from overeating, with a feeling of fullness in the chest and phlegm present. I administered Yigong San, and he recovered. Later, after overeating again, he suffered abdominal distension with pain. Even with medication taken to purge, although the pain ceased, the distension worsened and he experienced further wheezing. This indicated damage to the spleen's energy affecting the lungs, so I used Liu Jun, with Jie Geng for nourishment, and he recovered.

Another young child had abdominal distension, aversion to food, cold and heat sensations, and nausea, resembling an exterior wind attack. I noted that the pulse at the qi point was larger than at Renying, indicating stagnation of food and drink. I prescribed a dose of Baohe Wan, and all symptoms promptly receded. However, the abdominal distension persisted, so I treated with Yigong San, leading to recovery.

A young child suffering from a cold had a cough with phlegm. I treated him with Liu Jun, Jie Geng, Sang Pi, and Xing Ren, leading to recovery. Subsequently, he experienced stagnation of food and had symptoms of diarrhea, distension, and pain. I added Shan Zha and Hou Po to Liu Jun, which provided relief. When he then experienced vomiting from food stoppage, taking medication for purging worsened his cough. I suggested that this indicated a deficiency in both the spleen and lungs and needed adjustment and nourishment. He thought it was a slow treatment, so he took diaphoretic and purgative medicines instead, which exacerbated the previous symptoms and led to increased shaking of the head. I then used Tianma San, significantly adding Diaoteng Hook and Yigong San, and he ultimately recovered.[99p]

　　一小儿胸腹胀痛，寒热烦闷，以手按腹即哭，此饮食停滞也，先用保和丸一服，前证即愈。更加烦渴，按其腹不哭，此宿食去而脾气未复也，用五味异功散加柴胡治之而瘳。
　　一小儿饮食停滞，服消导之剂，饮食既消，热尚未退，此胃经虚热，用六君子加柴胡、升麻四剂而逾。
　　一小儿先因饮食停滞，服克伐之剂，更加腹痛，按之即止，余用六君子汤而愈。后复伤食，用保和丸及三棱、槟榔之类，更加腹重善噫，此脾气虚而下陷也，仍用前汤加升麻、柴胡、木香而愈。
　　一小儿面色青白，饮食难化，大便频泄，或用消积化痰等药，久不愈。余谓：脾胃虚弱也，用六君子汤渐愈。或以为食积，宜驱逐之，遂反作泻痰喘发搐。余谓：脾气复伤，不能生肺，肺虚不能平肝而作是证。先用六君子加钓藤钩，饮食少进；又用五味异功散加升麻而愈。[100p]

A child experiences abdominal swelling and pain, alternating between cold and heat, and cries when pressure is applied to the abdomen; this is due to food stagnation. First, administer a dose of Baohe Wan, and the symptoms will improve. If there is increased thirst and pressing on the abdomen does not cause crying, this indicates that the food has been eliminated but the spleen's qi has not yet recovered. Treat with Wuwei Yigong San, adding Chaihu, and the child will improve.

Another child has food stagnation and takes medication to dissolve it. Once the food has been digested, the heat has not yet subsided, indicating deficiency heat in the stomach channel. Use Liujunzi Tang with added Chaihu and Shengma for four doses to alleviate the condition.

A child who initially had food stagnation took medication to counteract it, but experienced increased abdominal pain; pressing stops the pain. The remaining treatment is with Liujunzi Decoction to achieve recovery. Later, there is renewed food injury; administer Baohe Wan along with Sanleng and Binglang. If there is increased heaviness in the abdomen with favorable belching, this points to deficient spleen qi leading to descent. Continue treating with the previous decoction, adding Shengma and Chaihu for recovery.

A child has a pale complexion, difficulty digesting food, and frequent diarrhea. Using medications for dissolving accumulation and transforming phlegm does not yield results over time. I suggest it is due to spleen and stomach weakness; use Liujunzi Tang to gradually improve. Some believe it to be food accumulation needing expulsion, which leads to diarrhea, phlegm, and spasms. I say the spleen qi is further harmed, unable to nourish the lungs, and the deficiency in the lungs cannot pacify the liver, causing these symptoms. First, use Liujunzi with added Diaoteng Gou, and restrict food intake; further use Wuwei Yigong San with added Shengma will lead to recovery.[100p]

　　一小儿患前证腹痛，服攻下之剂，发热不已，大便不化，按其腹不痛，与冷水不饮，此食积去而脾气虚也，用五味异功散加当归、升麻而愈。
　　一小儿患痞癖，服槟榔、蓬朮、枳实、黄连之类，痞益甚。余曰：此脾经血虚痞也，不可克伐。逐用六君子加当归，数剂胃气渐复，诸证渐愈。乃朝用异功散加升麻柴胡，夕用异功散加当归、芍药而愈。
　　一小儿患痞结，久而四肢消瘦，肚腹渐大，寒热嗜卧，作渴引饮，用白朮散为主，佐以四味肥儿丸，月余诸证渐愈。
　　一小儿患痞结，身热如火，病状多端，不可尽述，朝用五味异功散，夕用四味肥儿丸，月余诸证稍愈；佐以地黄丸，自能行立；遂朝用地黄丸，夕用异功散及虾(虫麻)丸，数服而愈。
[101p]

A young child suffered from abdominal pain due to heat accumulation, took a purgative, but continued to have a fever and undigested stools. Upon examination, there was no pain when pressing the abdomen, and the child refused cold water. This indicated that the food stagnation had resolved, but the spleen's energy was weak. A combination of the Five-Flavor Formula was prescribed with added Angelica and Cimicifuga, resulting in recovery.

Another young child had abdominal distension and took areca nut, dragon's blood, bitter orange, and coptis, which aggravated the distension. I said: This is due to deficiency in the spleen and blood stagnation; it should not be attacked directly. The Six Gentlemen Decoction with added Angelica was prescribed. After several doses, the stomach energy gradually recovered, and symptoms improved. In the morning, the Five-Flavor Formula with added Cimicifuga and Bupleurum was used, with the same formula plus Angelica and Peony in the evening, leading to recovery.

A different young child had a persistent abdominal blockage, became emaciated, and developed a growing abdomen, experienced chills and fever, was lethargic, and craved water. The main treatment was a formula based on Atractylodes, supplemented with Four-Flavor Fat Child Pills. After a month, various symptoms gradually improved.

Lastly, one child had abdominal blockage, felt hot like fire, exhibited various symptoms too extensive to detail, was treated with the Five-Flavor Formula in the morning and Four-Flavor Fat Child Pills in the evening. After a month, symptoms slightly improved; with the addition of Rehmannia Pills, the child could possibly walk. Consequently, Rehmannia Pills were used in the morning, and the Five-Flavor Formula along with Shrimp (or insect herb) Pills in the evening. After several doses, the child was cured.[101p]
